Definition and Origin of Tarawih Prayer
Defining the linguistic and technical meaning of 'tarwiha' and the origin of Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the linguistic and technical meanings of 'tarwiha' and state the origin of the name Tarawih.

Core Idea
Tarawih is named after the rest (tarwiha) taken after every four rak'ahs, not the prayer itself.

This hashya passage clarifies the etymology of 'Tarawih' – a term central to Ramadan nightly prayers. The commentator unpacks the term 'tarwiha' and its shift from a linguistic meaning (a rest) to a technical term for a set of rak'ahs. Understanding this origin helps us appreciate the prayer's structure and the Hanafi practice of including rests.

Guided Path
1
Isolate the term
Identify the word 'tarwiha' in the text and note its literal meaning.
The term appears in the context of the prayer's name.
2
Trace the semantic shift
Understand how the term moved from denoting a rest to denoting the four rak'ahs that precede the rest.
This is a metonymic transfer.
3
Connect to the prayer's name
Recognize that 'Tarawih' (plural of tarwiha) refers to the rests, and by extension the entire prayer.
The plural form indicates multiple rests.
4
Consider the missing report
Note that the text cuts off and the cited hadith is incomplete, but the lexical point remains clear.
The incomplete nature does not affect the definition given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة التراويح الترويحة الجلسة في الأصل، ثم سميت بها الأربع ركعات التي آخرها الترويحة روى
Section on the prayer of Tarawih. The 'tarwiha' is the sitting (jalsa) originally, then the four rak'ahs which end with the tarwiha are named after it. It was narrated...
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This is a brief definitional note from the hashya. The term 'tarwiha' linguistically means 'a single rest' (from raḥa, to rest). In the context of Salat al-Tarawih, it originally referred to the brief sitting after every four rak'ahs, during which participants would rest. Later, the entire set of four rak'ahs (or by extension, the whole prayer) came to be called Tarawih. The text cuts off before completing the isnad or report, but the lexical point is clear: the prayer's name derives from these intermissions.

Key Terms
الترويحة (al-tarwīḥa): A single rest or sitting; originally the short break after every four rak'ahs of the night prayer during Ramadan, then metaphorically applied to the four rak'ahs themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the word 'tarwiha' (singular of tarawih) originally mean?
A) The four rak'ahs of prayer.
B) The entire 20 rak'ahs.
C) The sitting (rest) after every four rak'ahs.
D) The recitation of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The name 'Tarawih' originates from the rests (tarwiha) taken after every four rak'ahs, not from the prayer itself.

Facing Qibla on a Moving Ship
Ruling on facing qibla during prayer on a moving ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for facing qibla during prayer on a moving ship and explain the ruling when the worshiper is unable to maintain direction.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is fard when able; it is waived when unable due to genuine hardship.

Praying on a moving ship presents a unique challenge: must one constantly face qibla even as the ship turns? The Hanafi school, known for its emphasis on ease, provides a nuanced answer based on the principle that obligations are contingent on ability. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its practical application, drawing on classical Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage discusses the act of facing qibla during prayer on a moving ship. Determine the default ruling (fard) and the key condition (ability).
2
Understand the Condition of Ability
Examine how the author links the obligation to the worshiper's ability. The phrase 'قدرته على فرض الاستقبال' is central.
Look for the term 'قدرة' (ability) and its implications.
3
Follow the Proof from Hanafi Texts
The author cites earlier works (al-Mudmarat, al-Isbijabi, al-Durar) to support the conditional view. Analyze how these authorities frame the rule.
The proof is based on the general principle that obligations are tied to capacity.
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The passage presents a differing view from Akmal al-Din, who argues for constant facing whenever able. Compare his position with the author's and note the rebuttal.
Focus on the concept of 'hardship' as a valid excuse.
5
Apply to Practical Scenarios
Consider real-world examples like a ship in a storm or a common ferry. Decide when facing is required and when it may be dropped or the prayer delayed.
The passage concludes that inability due to hardship excuses the requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كانت سائرة (يتوجه المصلي فيها للقبلة) لقدرته على فرض الاستقبال (عند افتتاح الصلاة وكلما استدارت) السفينة (عنها) أي القبلة (يتوجه) المصلي باستدارتها (إليها) أي القبلة (في خلال الصلاة) وإن عجز يمسك عن الصلاة (حتى) يقدر إلى أن (يتمها مستقبلاً) ولو ترك الاستقبال لا يجزيه في قولهم جميعاً. قوله: (وإن عجز الصلاة) نقله في الشرح عن مجمع الروايات . قوله : (ولو) ترك الاستقبال لا تجزيه في قولهم جميعاً) هذا ما أورده الشيخ أكمل الدين بقوله : وينبغي أن يتوجه إلى القبلة كيفما دارت السفينة سواء كان عند الإفتتاح، أو في خلال الصلاة لأنّ التوجه فرض عند القدرة، وهذا قادر اهـ كذا في الشرح قال بعض الحذاق المتبادر أن لزوم التوجه منوط بالقدرة عليه كما يشير إليه كلام المضمرات، والاسبيجابي إذ الاستقبال قد يسقط للعذر، ولو عند الإمكان كما في الخائف من عدوه عدم الإمكان أولى، والعلامة الأكمل لم يطلق لزوم الإستقبال، بل قيد بالقدرة، وعند عدم القدرة على الشيء كيف يتحقق لزومه، وإلى ما ذكرنا يشير كلام الدرر حيث قال: لأنه يمكنه الإستقبال من غير مشقة إذ مفهومه أنه عند عدم الإمكان، وعند المشقة لا يلزمه الاستقبال، ومفاهيم الكتب حجة كما لا يخفى وما في مجمع الروايات أنه إن عجز يمسك عن ا يمكن حمله على حالة الرجاء اهـ أي رجاء زوال العذر قبل الوقت فتأمل اهـ بتصرف، وهو كلام حسن إذ على ما أفاده المصنف يلزمه تأخير الصلوات في أسفار البحر الملح عند إشتداد الأرياح، وتقلبها، وفي سفن مصر عند السفر إلى العارف بالله تعالى السيد أحمد البدوي بحراً في المراكب العامة، وغير ذلك، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
If it (the ship) is moving, the worshiper in it faces the qibla because he is able to perform the obligation of facing it at the opening of the prayer and whenever the ship turns from it (i.e., the qibla), the worshiper turns with its turning towards it (the qibla) during the prayer. And if he is unable, he refrains from prayer until he is able to complete it facing the qibla. And if he leaves off facing the qibla, it does not suffice him according to all of them. His statement: “And if he is unable” is transmitted in the Sharh from Majma‘ al-Riwayat. His statement: “And if he leaves off facing the qibla, it does not suffice him according to all of them” – this is what Shaykh Akmal al-Din stated: “It is appropriate for him to face the qibla however the ship turns, whether at the beginning or during the prayer, because facing is an obligation when one is able, and this one is able.” This is in the Sharh. Some discerning scholars said: The obvious point is that the necessity of facing depends on ability, as indicated by the words of al-Mudmarat and al-Isbijabi, since facing may fall due to an excuse, even when possible – as in one who fears his enemy – then when incapable it is more appropriate. And al-‘Allama al-Akmal did not absolutely necessitate facing, but qualified it with ability, and when one cannot do something, how can its necessity be realized? The words of al-Durar point to what we mentioned: “Because he can face without hardship,” its implication being that when not possible or with hardship, facing is not required. And the concepts of books are evidence, as is not hidden. And what is in Majma‘ al-Riwayat that if unable he refrains from prayer can be interpreted as the case of hoping (for the excuse to disappear before the time), so ponder. This is good speech, because according to what the author stated, one would be required to delay prayers on salt sea voyages during strong and shifting winds, and on Egyptian ships traveling to the knower of Allah, Sayyid Ahmad al-Badawi, by sea on public boats, and other situations. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on prayer on a moving ship, specifically the requirement to face the qibla. The text states that if the ship is moving, the worshiper must face the qibla at the beginning of the prayer and whenever the ship turns away from it, turning with the ship to face it during the prayer. If he is unable to do so, he should stop praying until he is able to complete the prayer while facing the qibla. If he abandons facing the qibla, the prayer is not valid according to the consensus of the Hanafi imams. The discussion then addresses a nuance: some scholars, like Akmal al-Din, assert that facing is obligatory whenever able, even if the ship turns constantly. However, the author notes that the necessity of facing is contingent on ability; thus, if one is incapable due to hardship or lack of control, facing is not required. This is supported by references to other Hanafi works like al-Mudmarat and al-Isbijabi. The passage concludes with practical examples such as severe storms at sea, where delaying prayer may be necessary. The ruling is based on the principle that obligations are contingent on ability, and the Hanafi school prioritizes ease, as seen in the discussion of istihsan.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbāl al-qibla): Facing the direction of the Kaaba during prayer, a required condition for validity when able.
سائرة (sā'ira): A moving vessel, such as a ship, as opposed to stationary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should a worshiper on a moving ship face the qibla during prayer?
A) Only at the beginning of the prayer
B) Whenever the ship turns, if able
C) Only when the ship is stationary
D) Never, since the ship is moving

Key Takeaway
Facing qibla in prayer on a moving ship is fard when able; if unable due to hardship, the obligation is lifted and prayer may be delayed.

Definition and Ruling of Tarawih Prayer
Defining tarawih and establishing its ruling as sunnah muakkadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tarawih prayer, identify its ruling as sunnah muakkadah, and explain the proofs from the Prophet's practice and the Caliphs' consensus.

Core Idea
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah, established by the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions, not an innovation of 'Umar.

This lesson explores the definition and legal ruling of tarawih prayer, a special night prayer in Ramadan. We will examine the linguistic and technical meaning of 'tarawih,' the evidence for its status as sunnah muakkadah, and the resolution of an intra-Hanafi debate on its classification. The passage also addresses the number of rak'ahs and the authority of the rightly-guided caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic origin
Analyze how 'tarawih' (plural of tarwiha) originally meant 'sitting' or 'rest' and came to refer to sets of four rak'ahs after which a rest is taken.
The term is derived from the rest (istiraha) after each set of four rak'ahs.
2
Identify the ruling
Note the explicit statement that tarawih is 'sunnah muakkadah'. This is not a wajib or fard, but an emphasized sunnah the Prophet consistently performed.
The passage cites multiple sources (al-Khulasa, Asad al-Ikhtiyar) affirming this.
3
Examine the evidence
Review the primary proofs: the Prophet's own practice (as narrated by 'A'isha), the consensus of the Companions, and the action of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab in formalizing the congregation.
The Prophet stopped gathering for fear of obligation, but the practice continued individually.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi debate and resolution
Some later Hanafi scholars considered it mustahabb, but the report of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa settled the issue as sunnah.
This report (riwayah) is from the nawadir but accepted by the later authorities.
5
Discuss the number of rak'ahs
The Prophet's maximum was 11 (including witr), but the caliphs established 20 rak'ahs. The Hanafi school follows 20 based on the hadith 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs'.
The report of 20 from Ibn 'Abbas is considered weak, but 20 is confirmed by the practice of 'Umar and 'Uthman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في صلاة التراويح
قوله: (الترويحة الجلسة في الأصل، ثم سميت بها الأربع ركعات التي آخرها الترويحة روى) الحسن عن أبي حنيفة صفتها بقوله (التراويح سنة) كما في الخلاصة، أسد الاختيار، وروى بن عمرو عن أبي يوسف قال : سألت أبا حنيفة عن التراويح وما فعله عمر رضي الله عنه فقال : التراويح سنة مؤكدة، ولم يتخرصه عمر من تلقاء نفسه، ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً، ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهي سنة عين ركعات الخ) مجازا للإستراحة بعدها غالباً، فهو من إطلاق اسم المجاور على ما جاوره، وقوله : التي آخرها الأولى أن يقول التي بعدها ويمكن أن تكون نفسها راحة، ومنه قوله : أرحنا بالصلاة يا بلال أي أقمها فيكون فعلها راحة لأنّ إنتظارها مشقة على النفس، أو لأنها يتوصل بها إلى راحة الجنة وهذه العبارة التي للمصنف نقلها في الشرح عن المستصفي، والذي فيه عن الفتح أنّ التراويح ترويحة للنصف أي استراحة وهي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الإستراحة سميت بها كل أربع لاستلزامها شرعاً استراحة بعدها بقدرها اهـ فالعلاقة اللزوم. قوله : (التراويح (سنة) بإجماع الصحابة، ومن بعدهم من الأمة منكرها مبتدع ضال مردود الشهادة كما في المضمرات، وفي الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي . الله عنها أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى ذات ليلة في المسجد فصلى بصلاته ناس ثم صلى من القابلة فكثر الناس، ثم اجتمعوا من الليلة الثالثة والرابعة فلم يخرج إليهم رسول الله الله ، فلما أصبح قال : قد رأيت الذي صنعتم، فلم يمنعني من الخروج إليكم إلا أني خشيت أن تفرض عليكم»، وفي الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما كان رسول الله الله يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة اهـ منها الوتر كما في صحيحي ابن خزيمة وابن حبان، وأما ما رواه ابن أبي شيبة، والطبراني، والبيهقي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه كان يصلي في رمضان عشرين سوى الوتر فضعيف، وإنما ثبت العشرون بمواظبة الخلفاء الراشدين ما عدا الصديق رضي | تعالى عنهم : ففي البخاري : فتوفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والأمر على ذلك في خلافة أبي بكر، وصدر خلافة عمر حين جمعهم عمر على أبي بن كعب فقام بهم في رمضان فكان ذلك أول اجتماع الناس على قارىء واحد في رمضان كما في فتح الباري، وبالجملة فهي سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سنها لنا وندبنا إليها وكيف لا وقد قال : عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين من بعدي عضوا عليها بالنواجذ، وروى أبو نعيم من حديث عروبة الكندي أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : استحدث بعدي أشياء فأحبها إلي أن تلزموا ما أحدث عمر، وفي البحر عن الخلاصة اختلف المشايخ في كونها سنة يعني أو مستحبة قال : وانقطع الخلاف برواية الحسن عن الإمام أنها سنة اهـ وقد ذكر الأصوليون أن السنة ما فعله النبي ،، أو واحد من الصحابة . قوله: (ولم يتخرصه عمر من : تلقاء نفسه) قال في القاموس : تخرصه افترى عليه اهـ وقال
Chapter on Tarawih Prayer. His statement: (Al-tarwiha originally means sitting, then it came to refer to the four rak‘ahs at the end of which is a rest. It is reported by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa describing it with his statement: (Tarawih is sunnah) as in al-Khulasa, Asad al-Ikhtiyar. And Ibn ‘Amr reported from Abu Yusuf: I asked Abu Hanifa about tarawih and what ‘Umar did, and he said: Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah; ‘Umar did not fabricate it from himself, nor was he an innovator in it, nor did he command it except on a basis he had and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah. It is a personal sunnah of rak‘ahs, metaphorically for the rest after them usually. It is giving the name of the adjacent thing to what is adjacent. And his statement: “at the end of which” – it would be better to say “after which”. And it can be that it is itself a rest, from his saying: “Give us rest with the prayer, O Bilal,” i.e., perform it, so doing it is a rest because waiting is a hardship on the soul, or because it leads to the rest of Paradise. This expression of the author is transmitted in the Sharh from al-Mustasfa, and in it from al-Fath that tarawih is a rest for half, i.e., a break, and originally is a verbal noun meaning rest; it is named for every four (rak‘ahs) because it necessitates a rest after them equal to them. So the relationship is necessity. His statement: (Tarawih is sunnah) by consensus of the Companions and those after them from the Ummah; one who denies it is an innovator, misguided, his testimony rejected. In the Sahihayn from ‘A’isha that the Messenger of Allah prayed one night in the mosque and people prayed with him, then on the next night people increased, then on the third and fourth nights they gathered but he did not come out to them. In the morning he said: “I saw what you did; nothing prevented me from coming out to you except that I feared it would be made obligatory upon you.” And in the Sahihayn from ‘A’isha: The Messenger of Allah never exceeded eleven rak‘ahs in Ramadan or otherwise, including witr. As for the report of Ibn Abi Shayba, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi that Ibn ‘Abbas prayed twenty rak‘ahs besides witr, it is weak. Twenty is confirmed by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs except Abu Bakr. In Bukhari: The Messenger of Allah died and the matter remained that way during Abu Bakr’s caliphacy and the beginning of ‘Umar’s, until ‘Umar gathered them behind Ubayy ibn Ka‘b and he led them in Ramadan, and that was the first time people gathered behind one reciter in Ramadan. In summary, it is the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah; he legislated it for us and recommended it. How could it not be, when he said: “Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs after me; cling to it with your molar teeth.” And Abu Nu‘aym narrated from ‘Uruwa al-Kindi that the Messenger of Allah said: “Things will be invented after me, and the most beloved to me is that you adhere to what ‘Umar innovated.” In al-Bahr from al-Khulasa: The scholars differed whether it is sunnah or mustahabb. He said: The difference was resolved by the report of al-Hasan from the Imam that it is sunnah. And the usul scholars have stated that sunnah is what the Prophet or one of the Companions did. His statement: (And ‘Umar did not fabricate it from himself). He said in al-Qamus: takharusahu means he lied against him. And he said...
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage defines tarawih prayer and establishes its ruling. The term 'tarawih' originally means 'sitting' but then came to refer to sets of four rak‘ahs because of the rest taken after them. The prayer is declared a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) based on the practice of the Prophet, the consensus of the Companions, and the action of ‘Umar. The text cites a report from Abu Hanifa affirming it as sunnah, refuting any notion that ‘Umar innovated it. Evidence from the Sahihayn shows that the Prophet prayed it in congregation but stopped fearing it would become obligatory. The number of rak‘ahs is discussed: the Prophet’s practice was eleven rak‘ahs (including witr), but the twenty rak‘ahs are established by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs (except Abu Bakr). The passage emphasizes that tarawih is a sunnah of the Prophet and the caliphs, and denying it is considered misguided. The report of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa settles the debate over whether it is sunnah or mustahabb.

Key Terms
تراويح (taráwīḥ): The night prayer in Ramadan, consisting of multiple sets of rak‘ahs, called tarawih because of the rest taken after each set.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah, a practice the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged; its omission is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of tarawih prayer?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mustahabb
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah, rooted in the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions, and its performance in 20 rak'ahs follows the practice of the rightly-guided caliphs.

Tarawih: A Confirmed Sunnah – Rulings and Proofs
Establishes Tarawih as Sunnah Mu'akkadah with proofs and congregational ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Tarawih is Sunnah Mu'akkadah, cite the primary proof from the Prophet's action, and explain why congregation is Sunnah Kifayah.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a Prophetic Sunnah, not Umar's innovation, and its congregation is a collective duty.

In this passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, we explore the legal status of Tarawih prayer. The author affirms it is a confirmed Sunnah (Sunnah Mu'akkadah), firmly rooted in the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the Companions. We will examine the proofs, including the famous hadith of Aisha, and understand why congregation in Tarawih is a Sunnah Kifayah, not an individual obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the explicit statement that Tarawih is Sunnah Mu'akkadah. Note that this is affirmed by Abu Hanifa and settled by the narration of al-Hasan.
The passage quotes Abu Hanifa directly: 'Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah.'
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith in the two Sahihs from Aisha: the Prophet prayed Tarawih in congregation for three nights then stopped, saying he feared it would become obligatory.
This shows it is a recommended act, not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's fear of obligation indicates the act is mustahabb, not obligatory. The explicit statement 'I feared it would be made obligatory' proves it is not fard.
Also, the hadith 'Hold fast to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs' makes the practice of the caliphs a Sunnah.
4
Analyze the dispute
The passage refutes two claims: (1) Rafidah deny Tarawih or say it is only for men; (2) Some attribute it solely to Umar. The Hanafi response: it is the Prophet's Sunnah, and Umar acted on a Prophetic precedent.
The dispute was settled by al-Hasan's narration from Abu Hanifa.
5
Understand the congregation ruling
The passage states that praying Tarawih in congregation is Sunnah Kifayah: if enough people do it, the rest are absolved; if all abandon, all are blameworthy. Al-Marghinani's view of Sunnah 'Ayn is set aside; the fatwa is on the dislike of the imam leading twice.
This is a key point: the community obligation vs individual.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة
وهي مؤكدة كما في الحسن عن أبي حنيفة صفتها بقوله (التراويح سنة) كما في الخلاصة، أسد الاختيار، وروى بن عمرو عن أبي يوسف قال : سألت أبا حنيفة عن التراويح وما فعله عمر رضي الله عنه فقال : التراويح سنة مؤكدة، ولم يتخرصه عمر من تلقاء نفسه، ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً، ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهي سنة عين. ركعات الخ) مجازا للإستراحة بعدها غالباً، فهو من إطلاق اسم المجاور على ما جاوره، وقوله : التي آخرها الأولى أن يقول التي بعدها ويمكن أن تكون نفسها راحة، ومنه قوله : أرحنا بالصلاة يا بلال أي أقمها فيكون فعلها راحة لأنّ إنتظارها مشقة على النفس، أو لأنها يتوصل بها إلى راحة الجنة وهذه العبارة التي للمصنف نقلها في الشرح عن المستصفي، والذي فيه عن الفتح أنّ التراويح ترويحة للنصف أي استراحة وهي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الإستراحة سميت بها كل أربع لاستلزامها شرعاً استراحة بعدها بقدرها اهـ فالعلاقة اللزوم. قوله : (التراويح (سنة) بإجماع الصحابة، ومن بعدهم من الأمة منكرها مبتدع ضال مردود الشهادة كما في المضمرات، وفي الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي . الله عنها أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى ذات ليلة في المسجد فصلى بصلاته ناس ثم صلى من القابلة فكثر الناس، ثم اجتمعوا من الليلة الثالثة والرابعة فلم يخرج إليهم رسول الله الله ، فلما أصبح قال : قد رأيت الذي صنعتم، فلم يمنعني من الخروج إليكم إلا أني خشيت أن تفرض عليكم»، وفي الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها ما كان رسول الله الله يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة اهـ منها الوتر كما في صحيحي ابن خزيمة وابن حبان، وأما ما رواه ابن أبي شيبة، والطبراني، والبيهقي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه كان يصلي في رمضان عشرين سوى الوتر فضعيف، وإنما ثبت العشرون بمواظبة الخلفاء الراشدين ما عدا الصديق رضي | تعالى عنهم : ففي البخاري : فتوفي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم والأمر على ذلك في خلافة أبي بكر، وصدر خلافة عمر حين جمعهم عمر على أبي بن كعب فقام بهم في رمضان فكان ذلك أول اجتماع الناس على قارىء واحد في رمضان كما في فتح الباري، وبالجملة فهي سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سنها لنا وندبنا إليها وكيف لا وقد قال : عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين من بعدي عضوا عليها بالنواجذ، وروى أبو نعيم من حديث عروبة الكندي أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : استحدث بعدي أشياء فأحبها إلي أن تلزموا ما أحدث عمر، وفي البحر عن الخلاصة اختلف المشايخ في كونها سنة يعني أو مستحبة قال : وانقطع الخلاف برواية الحسن عن الإمام أنها سنة اهـ وقد ذكر الأصوليون أن السنة ما فعله النبي ،، أو واحد من الصحابة . قوله: (ولم يتخرصه عمر من : تلقاء نفسه) قال في القاموس : تخرصه افترى عليه اهـ وقال من

مؤكدة على الرجال والنساء) ثبتت سنيتها بفعل النبي ، وقوله قال : عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين من بعدي وقد واظب عليها ،عمر وعثمان وعلي رضي الله عنهم وقال في حديث افترض الله عليكم صيامه وسننت لكم قيامه وفيه رد لقول بعض الروافض هي سنة الرجال دون النساء وقول بعضهم سنة عمر لأن الصحيح أنها سنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والجماعة سنة فيها أيضاً لكن على الكفاية بينه بقوله (وصلاتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية لما ثبت أنه صلى بالجماعة إحدى عشرة ركعة بالوتر على سبيل التداعي ولم مجری سائر النوافل، ثم بين العذر في الترك وهو خشيته افتراضها علينا، وقال يجره عن قبله : الخرص القول بالظن، وذكر له معاني كثيرة. قوله في حديث بالتنكير، وقوله افترض الخ في محل نصب مقول القول. قوله : (وفيه رد لقول بعض الروافض هي سنة الرجال دون النساء) أقول هكذا قاله حافظ الدين في الكافي لكن المشهور عنهم أنها ليست بسنة أصلاً قال في البرهان قد اجتمعت الأمة على مشروعية التراويح وجوازها، ولم ينكرها أحد من أهل القبلة إلا الروافض ذكره العلامة نوح قوله : (وقول بعضهم سنة عمر الخ) في الفتاوي الهندية الجواهر . هي سنة رسول الله ، وقيل : هي سنة عمر رضي الله عنه، والأول أصح، وفي حاشية السيد على العلامة مسكين وما قيل يكفر من يقول إنها سنة عمر رضي الله عنه كما تقوله الروافض فممنوع، فقد صرح في كثير من المتداولات بأنها سنة عمر يعني بالنظر لكونها عشرين ركعة، وللمواظبة عليها، وذلك لا يمنع كونها سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أيضاً لما ذكرنا اهـ . قوله : (وصلاتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية فلا لو على من لم يحضر الجماعة إلا أن يتركوها جميعاً أو يكون فقيهاً يقتدى به وقال المرغيناني إنها سنة عين وكره أن يؤم في التراويح مرتين في ليلة واحدة وعليه الفتوى لأن السنة لا تتكرر في الوقت الواحد، فتقع الثانية نفلاً مضمرات بخلاف ما لو صلاها مأموماً مرتين حيث لا يكره كما لو أم فيها، ثم اقتدى بآخر في تلك الصلاة، وكما لو صلى العشاء إماماً، أو مقتدياً، ثم أقيمت ثانياً فإنه لا يكره له أن يدخل فيها ثانياً، بل يستحل له ذلك كما حققه العمدة ابن أمير حاج، ولينظر الجمع بين هذا، من حديث لا يصلي بعد صلاة ،مثلها، والظاهر أن الظهر مثل العشاء بخلاف بقية الفرائض فيكره إعادتها، وهذا غير مشهور فإنّ المشهور كراهة الإعادة إلا لمن صلى منفرداً، ثم أقيمت صلاة العشاء، أو الظهر، ويستفاد من طلب الجماعة في التراويح أن فضيلتها بالجماعة أكثر من فضيلة الإنفراد، وهل هي كالجماعة في الفرض، فتضاعف على صلاة الفذ وعشرين، أو خمس بسبع وعشرين، أو المتحقق فيها زيادة ثواب من غير قيد بالعدد، ومثل ذلك يقال في صلاة التطوع : جماعة إذا كان على غير وجه التداعي يحرر قوله : (وهو) خشيته افتراضها علينا) إن قيل كيف خشي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تفترض علينا مع علمه بأنه لا يزاد على الصلوات الخمس لقوله تعالى في حديث الإسراء لما فرض الصلاة لا يبدل القول لديّ أجيب بأن الممنوع زيادة الأوقات
Book of Prayer. And it is confirmed as in al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: its description by his saying: 'Tarawih is sunnah' as in al-Khulasa, Asad al-Ikhtiyar. And Ibn Amr narrated from Abu Yusuf who said: I asked Abu Hanifa about Tarawih and what Umar did, may Allah be pleased with him. He said: Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah, and Umar did not fabricate it from himself, nor was he an innovator in it, and he only commanded it based on a principle he had and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And it is a sunnah 'ayn. (The word 'rak'at' is metaphorical for the rest after them usually, so it is applying the name of the adjacent to what it is adjacent to. And his saying: 'which is last' it is better to say 'which comes after' and it can be itself rest, and from it his saying: 'Give us rest with prayer, O Bilal' meaning establish it, so performing it is rest because waiting for it is hardship on the soul, or because it leads to the rest of Paradise. And this expression of the author transmitted in the Sharh from al-Mustasfa, and what is in it from al-Fath that Tarawih is a tarwiha for half, meaning a rest, and it is originally a verbal noun meaning rest, named for every four because it necessitates legally a rest after it equal to it. So the relation is of necessity. His saying: (Tarawih is sunnah) by consensus of the Companions and those after them of the Ummah; its denier is an innovator, misguided, rejected testimony as in al-Mudmarat. And in the two Sahihs from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, prayed one night in the mosque, and people prayed with his prayer, then he prayed the next night and many people came, then they gathered on the third and fourth night but the Messenger of Allah did not come out to them. When morning came he said: 'I saw what you did, and nothing prevented me from coming out to you except that I feared it would be made obligatory upon you.' And in the two Sahihs from Aisha: 'The Messenger of Allah would not increase in Ramadan or otherwise beyond eleven rak'ahs' including witr as in the Sahihs of Ibn Khuzayma and Ibn Hibban. As for what was narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas that he used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan besides witr, it is weak. Rather, twenty is established by the constant practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs except Abu Bakr. In al-Bukhari: The Messenger of Allah died and the matter continued thus in the caliphate of Abu Bakr and the beginning of Umar's caliphate, until Umar gathered them upon Ubayy ibn Ka'b and he led them in prayer in Ramadan, and that was the first gathering of people upon one reciter in Ramadan as in Fath al-Bari. In summary, it is the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, which he prescribed for us and called us to. How could it not be, when he said: 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after me, bite onto it with your molars.' And Abu Nu'aym narrated from the hadith of Urwa al-Kindi that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Things will be innovated after me, and the most beloved to me is that you adhere to what Umar innovated.' And in al-Bahr from al-Khulasa: The scholars differed on whether it is sunnah (meaning recommended) and he said: The dispute was ended by the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam that it is sunnah. And the usuliyyun have mentioned that sunnah is what the Prophet or one of the Companions did. His saying: 'and Umar did not fabricate it from himself' - in al-Qamus: 'takharrasahu' he slandered him. And he said from before him: al-kharas is speaking by conjecture, and he mentioned many meanings for it. His saying: 'confirmed upon men and women' - its sunniyah is established by the Prophet's action and his saying: 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after me.' And Umar, Uthman, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them, were constant upon it. And he said in a hadith: 'Allah has obligated upon you its fasting and I have prescribed for you its standing (prayer).' In it is a refutation of the saying of some Rafidah that it is sunnah for men not women, and the saying of some that it is the sunnah of Umar, because the correct view is that it is the sunnah of the Prophet. And congregation in it is also sunnah, but on the basis of sufficiency (kifayah). He clarified that by his saying: (And praying it in congregation is a sunnah kifayah) because it is established that he prayed in congregation eleven rak'ahs with witr on the basis of invitation (tada'i) and he did not make it like other supererogatory prayers. Then he explained the excuse for leaving it, which was his fear that it would be made obligatory upon us. His saying: 'and he did not make it like other supererogatory prayers' - the meaning is that he did not make it like them in terms of congregation being disliked. Then he explained that the Prophet left it out of fear of obligation. His saying in the hadith with the indefinite article, and his saying 'obligated' is in the accusative case as the content of the saying. His saying: (And in it is a refutation of the saying of some Rafidah that it is sunnah for men not women). I say: Thus said Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi, but the well-known from them is that it is not sunnah at all. Al-Burhan said: The Ummah has agreed on the legitimacy and permissibility of Tarawih, and no one among the people of the Qibla has denied it except the Rafidah. Mentioned by Allama Nuh. His saying: (And the saying of some that it is the sunnah of Umar etc.) In al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya and al-Jawahir: It is the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, and it is said it is the sunnah of Umar, and the first is more correct. And in the Hashiya of al-Sayyid on Allama Miskin: What is said that whoever says it is the sunnah of Umar is a disbeliever, as the Rafidah say, is prohibited. For it is stated in many commonly circulated works that it is the sunnah of Umar, meaning with regard to being twenty rak'ahs and constant practice upon it, and that does not prevent it from being the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah as well, for what we have mentioned. His saying: (And praying it in congregation is a sunnah kifayah) so it is not disliked for one who does not attend the congregation unless they all leave it or he is a jurist who is followed. Al-Marghinani said: It is a sunnah 'ayn, and he disliked that a person lead in Tarawih twice in one night, and upon that is the fatwa, because the sunnah is not repeated in one time, so the second occurs as nafl. Al-Mudmarat: contrary to if he prays it as a follower twice, where it is not disliked, as if he led in it then followed another in that same prayer, and as if he prayed Isha as an imam or follower, then another congregation was established, it is not disliked for him to enter it a second time, rather it is recommended for him as verified by the pillar Ibn Amir Haj. And it is necessary to reconcile this with the hadith 'Do not pray after a prayer its like.' The apparent is that Zuhr is like Isha, unlike the other obligatory prayers, so repeating them is disliked. And this is not well-known, for the well-known is the dislike of repetition except for one who prayed alone then an Isha or Zuhr congregation is established. And it is derived from the request of congregation in Tarawih that its virtue in congregation is greater than the virtue of praying alone. And is it like congregation in obligatory prayer, so it is multiplied over the prayer of an individual by twenty, or twenty-seven, or is it established that there is an increase in reward without restriction of number? And something similar is said about supererogatory prayer in congregation when it is not on the basis of invitation. It needs verification. His saying: (and it is his fear that it would be made obligatory upon us) If it is said: How could the Prophet fear that it would be made obligatory upon us when he knew that nothing would be added to the five prayers due to His saying in the hadith of the Night Journey when prayer was made obligatory: 'The word is not changed with Me'? The answer: What is prohibited is the increase of times.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah is a critical refinement of the rules concerning Tarawih prayer. The author begins by affirming that Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah (Sunnah Mu'akkadah), quoting Abu Hanifa's response to Abu Yusuf. Abu Hanifa explicitly states that Umar did not innovate Tarawih from his own opinion but acted upon a foundation from the Prophet. The text then discusses the etymology of 'Tarawih' (from tarwiha meaning rest), indicating that the name is given because of the rest after every four rak'ahs.

The ruling that Tarawih is Sunnah is supported by the consensus of the Companions and later scholars; its denier is considered an innovator and misguided, with his testimony rejected. The proof includes the hadith in the Sahihayn where the Prophet feared that Tarawih would become obligatory, and the hadith that he did not exceed eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan (including witr). The claim of twenty rak'ahs from Ibn Abbas is deemed weak; rather, twenty is established by the constant practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after the Prophet's death, as recorded in Bukhari. The author emphasizes that Tarawih is the Prophet's Sunnah, citing the hadith 'Hold fast to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs' and a hadith that adherence to what Umar introduced is beloved.

An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: some scholars debated whether Tarawih is Sunnah or merely mustahabb, but the matter was settled by the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa that it is Sunnah. The author then refutes the Rafidah claim that Tarawih is only for men, confirming it is for both men and women. Another refutation addresses the claim that Tarawih is the Sunnah of Umar alone; the correct view is that it is the Prophet's Sunnah, though the practice of twenty rak'ahs and constant vigilance is attributed to Umar, which does not negate its Prophetic origin.

Regarding congregation, the text states that praying Tarawih in congregation is Sunnah Kifayah (sufficiency). This means if some perform it in congregation, the obligation on the rest falls. If everyone abandons it, they are blameworthy. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: al-Marghinani considers it Sunnah 'Ayn (individual), but the author notes that the fatwa is on the dislike of an imam leading Tarawih twice in one night because the Sunnah is not repeated; the second becomes nafl. However, if a person prays as a follower twice, it is not disliked. The passage also discusses the virtue of congregation in Tarawih and compares it to obligatory prayer, noting that there is an increase in reward but without specifying a multiplier. Finally, the author addresses an objection: how could the Prophet fear obligation when it is established that no prayer times are added beyond five? The response is that the prohibition of increase refers to the number of times (i.e., daily prayer times), not the number of rak'ahs within a time.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): The supererogatory night prayer in Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs (in the Hanafi school), prayed in congregation.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed Sunnah; an act the Prophet regularly performed and encouraged, but omission does not incur sin, though it is blameworthy to leave it habitually.
سنة كفاية (sunnah kifāyah): A Sunnah that is collectively obligatory: if enough people perform it, the rest are absolved; if all abandon it, all are blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of praying Tarawih in congregation according to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah 'Ayn (individual obligation)
B) Sunnah Kifayah (collective sufficiency)
C) Wajib (obligatory)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah (Sunnah Mu'akkadah) for men and women, and its performance in congregation is a collective duty (Sunnah Kifayah), not an individual obligation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Tarawih: Sunnah Muakkadah and Its Congregation as Sunnah Kifayah
Establishes the sunnah status of Tarawih and the collective nature of its congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tarawih prayer, identify its proof from sunnah, and distinguish between sunnah 'ayn and sunnah kifayah regarding its congregation.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah for all; its congregation is a collective sunnah, not individually obligatory.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih prayer. The passage establishes that it is a confirmed sunnah for both men and women, backing it with prophetic proof and refuting erroneous claims. We will explore why its congregation is considered sunnah kifayah and the implications for individual and communal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Tarawih prayer. What is the hukm? Sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) for both men and women.
The text emphasizes that it is not merely a sunnah of Umar but of the Prophet.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The Prophet's action and his sayings: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs' and 'Allah has obligated you to fast it and I have prescribed its standing.'
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it suffices for sunnah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How do the proofs indicate sunnah? The imperative 'alaykum' indicates recommendation, not obligation. The phrase 'sanantu lakum' indicates prophetic prescription (sunnah).
Thus, the proof establishes sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars like al-Marghinani consider congregation for Tarawih as sunnah 'ayn, while the majority view is sunnah kifayah.
The author prefers sunnah kifayah, citing evidence from Companions who prayed individually.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that congregation is sunnah kifayah, so if enough people pray in the mosque, the sunnah is fulfilled for all.
However, praying in the mosque is still better than at home.

سنة كفاية لما ثبت أنه صلى بالجماعة إحدى عشرة ركعة بالوتر على سبيل التداعي ولم مجری سائر النوافل، ثم بين العذر في الترك وهو خشيته افتراضها علينا، وقال يجره عن قبله : الخرص القول بالظن، وذكر له معاني كثيرة. قوله في حديث بالتنكير، وقوله افترض الخ في محل نصب مقول القول. قوله : (وفيه رد لقول بعض الروافض هي سنة الرجال دون النساء) أقول هكذا قاله حافظ الدين في الكافي لكن المشهور عنهم أنها ليست بسنة أصلاً قال في البرهان قد اجتمعت الأمة على مشروعية التراويح وجوازها، ولم ينكرها أحد من أهل القبلة إلا الروافض ذكره العلامة نوح قوله : (وقول بعضهم سنة عمر الخ) في الفتاوي الهندية الجواهر . هي سنة رسول الله ، وقيل : هي سنة عمر رضي الله عنه، والأول أصح، وفي حاشية السيد على العلامة مسكين وما قيل يكفر من يقول إنها سنة عمر رضي الله عنه كما تقوله الروافض فممنوع، فقد صرح في كثير من المتداولات بأنها سنة عمر يعني بالنظر لكونها عشرين ركعة، وللمواظبة عليها، وذلك لا يمنع كونها سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أيضاً لما ذكرنا اهـ . قوله : (وصلاتها بالجماعة سنة كفاية فلا لو على من لم يحضر الجماعة إلا أن يتركوها جميعاً أو يكون فقيهاً يقتدى به وقال المرغيناني إنها سنة عين وكره أن يؤم في التراويح مرتين في ليلة واحدة وعليه الفتوى لأن السنة لا تتكرر في الوقت الواحد، فتقع الثانية نفلاً مضمرات بخلاف ما لو صلاها مأموماً مرتين حيث لا يكره كما لو أم فيها، ثم اقتدى بآخر في تلك الصلاة، وكما لو صلى العشاء إماماً، أو مقتدياً، ثم أقيمت ثانياً فإنه لا يكره له أن يدخل فيها ثانياً، بل يستحل له ذلك كما حققه العمدة ابن أمير حاج، ولينظر الجمع بين هذا، من حديث لا يصلي بعد صلاة ،مثلها، والظاهر أن الظهر مثل العشاء بخلاف بقية الفرائض فيكره إعادتها، وهذا غير مشهور فإنّ المشهور كراهة الإعادة إلا لمن صلى منفرداً، ثم أقيمت صلاة العشاء، أو الظهر، ويستفاد من طلب الجماعة في التراويح أن فضيلتها بالجماعة أكثر من فضيلة الإنفراد، وهل هي كالجماعة في الفرض، فتضاعف على صلاة الفذ وعشرين، أو خمس بسبع وعشرين، أو المتحقق فيها زيادة ثواب من غير قيد بالعدد، ومثل ذلك يقال في صلاة التطوع : جماعة إذا كان على غير وجه التداعي يحرر قوله : (وهو) خشيته افتراضها علينا) إن قيل كيف خشي النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تفترض علينا مع علمه بأنه لا يزاد على الصلوات الخمس لقوله تعالى في حديث الإسراء لما فرض الصلاة لا يبدل القول لديّ أجيب بأن الممنوع زيادة الأوقات وبين ما ورد الصدر الشهيد الجماعة سنة كفاية فيها حتى لو أقامها البعض في المسجد بجماعة وباقي أهل المحلة أقامها منفرداً في بيته لا يكون تاركاً للسنة لأنه يروى عن أفراد الصحابة التخلف، وقال في المبسوط : لو صلي إنسان في بيته لا يأثم فقد فعله ابن عمر وعروة، وسالم والقاسم وابراهيم، ونافع فدل فعل هؤلاء أن الجماعة في المسجد سنة على سبيل الكفاية إذ لا يظن بابن عمر ومن تبعه ترك السنة انتهى وإن صلاها بجماعة في بيته فالصحيح أنه نال إحدى الفضيلتين فإن الأداء في المسجد له فضيلة ليس للأداء في البيت ذلك وكذا الحكم في الفرائض
The Book of Prayer. (Tarawih is) a confirmed sunnah upon men and women. Its sunniyah is established by the action of the Prophet and his saying: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs after me.' And Umar, Uthman, and Ali adhered to it. And he said in a hadith: 'Allah has obligated you to fast it (Ramadan) and I have prescribed for you its standing (in prayer).' In this is a refutation of the saying of some Rafidah that it is a sunnah for men only, and the saying of some that it is the sunnah of Umar, because the correct view is that it is the sunnah of the Prophet himself. Congregational prayer in it is also sunnah, but on the level of kifayah. He clarified that by his saying: 'And its prayer in congregation is sunnah kifayah because it is established that he prayed eleven rak'ahs with congregation including witr by way of mutual summons, and it was not conducted like other supererogatory prayers.' Then he explained the excuse for its abandonment: his fear that it would become obligatory upon us. And he said... (then comments and refutations)... The Chief Martyr said: Congregation in it is sunnah kifayah, so that if some people pray it in the mosque with congregation and the rest of the people of the neighborhood pray it individually in their homes, they are not abandoning the sunnah, because it is narrated that individual Companions stayed away. And it is said in al-Mabsut: If a person prays in his home, he does not sin; Ibn Umar, Urwa, Salim, Qasim, Ibrahim, and Nafi' did that. Their actions indicate that congregation in the mosque is sunnah on the basis of sufficiency, for it is not thought that Ibn Umar and those who followed him abandoned the sunnah. And if he prays it with congregation in his home, the correct view is that he attains one of the two virtues: performance in the mosque has a virtue that performance at home does not. The same rule applies to obligatory prayers.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiya) on the rulings of Tarawīh prayer. It begins by asserting that Tarawīh is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for both men and women, contrary to the Rafidah who claim it is only for men. The proof is the Prophet's action and his command to follow his sunnah and that of the caliphs. The text refutes the notion that it is merely the sunnah of 'Umar by clarifying that the Prophet himself instituted it. The congregation for Tarawīh is ruled as sunnah kifāyah (collective sunnah), meaning that if enough people pray it in congregation in the mosque, the obligation of the sunnah is fulfilled for the community. However, scholars like al-Marghinānī considered it sunnah 'ayn (individual sunnah). The author notes that the Prophet initially avoided regular congregation out of fear that it would become obligatory, but this fear ended with his death. The commentary then discusses the virtue of praying Tarawīh in congregation versus individually, and addresses the issue of repeating the Tarawīh prayer—it is disliked for the imam to lead it twice in one night, but not for a follower to pray it twice. The passage emphasizes that congregational prayer in the mosque is superior, though praying at home with congregation still earns one virtue.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarāwīḥ): The night prayer of Ramadan, consisting of twenty rak'ahs, prayed after Isha, which is a confirmed sunnah.
سنة كفاية (sunnat kifāyah): A sunnah whose fulfillment by some members of the community absolves others of responsibility; if no one performs it, all are blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of congregational prayer for Tarawih?
A) It is fard
B) It is sunnah muakkadah for each individual
C) It is sunnah kifayah
D) It is makruh

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed sunnah for all Muslims, and its congregational prayer is a collective sunnah, not individually obligatory, though praying in congregation is more virtuous.

Timing of Tarawih and Sequence with Witr
Determines the time for Tarawih and the ruling on offering Witr before it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct time for Tarawih, explain the ruling on offering Witr before Tarawih, and identify the Hanafi position on making up missed Tarawih.

Core Idea
Tarawih time is after Isha until dawn; Witr after Tarawih is better; missed Tarawih is not made up.

This lesson clarifies the precise time for performing Tarawih prayers and the proper sequence with Witr. The Hanafi school has a detailed ruling based on the connection of Tarawih to Isha, as well as a firm stance on whether missed Tarawih can be compensated. We will walk through the main ruling, the reasoning behind it, and a notable intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time of Tarawih
State the correct time according to the majority Hanafi view: after Isha until dawn.
The text says 'al-sahih' for after Isha.
2
Understand the sequence with Witr
Explain that Witr may be offered before or after Tarawih, but delaying it until after Tarawih is better. Also note the scenario where Isha is later found invalid: Isha and Tarawih are repeated, but Witr is not, as it becomes a nafl prayer.
3
Consider the minority view
Isma'il al-Zahid and others hold that the entire night (including before Isha) is valid for Tarawih because it is qiyam al-layl.
This view is not adopted as mufta bihi.
4
Examine the ruling on making up missed Tarawih
State that the correct view is that missed Tarawih are not made up at all; if one prays them later, they count as nafl, not Tarawih.
The text says 'as-sahih annaha la tuqda mutlaqan'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ووقتها) ما (بعد صلاة العشاء على الصحيح إلى طلوع الفجر (و) لتبعيتها للعشاء (يصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح وتأخيره عنه وهو أفضل حتى لو تبين فساد العشاء دون التراويح والوتر أعادوا العشاء ثم التراويح دون الوتر عند أبي حنيفة بوقوعها نافلة مطلقة بوقوعها في غير محلها هو الصحيح، وقال جماعة من أصحابنا . منهم إسمعيل الزاهد أن الليل كله وقت لها قبل العشاء وبعده وقبل الوتر وبعده لأنها قيام الليل (ويستحب تأخير التراويح إلى قبيل ثلث الليل (أو) قبيل (نصفه) واختلفوا في أدائها بعد النصف فقال بعضهم : يكره لأنها تبع للعشاء فصارت كسنة العشاء (و) قال بعضهم: (لا يكره تأخيرها ونقصانها لا زيادة عدد الركعات ونقصانها ألا ترى أن الصلاة فرضت ركعتين فأقرت في السفر وزيدت في الحضر كما في حاشية الشلبي على الزيلعي أو أنّ الفرضية قد تكون معلقة على المداومة، أو خشيت بمداومة عليها أن تعتقد وفرضيتها اهـ. قوله: (وباقي أهل المحلة أقامها منفرداً أفاد بهذا التعبير أنها سنة كفاية لكل محلة فيها مسجد فإقامتها بمسجد واحد في البلد لا تسقط الجماعة عن جميعهم حيث تعددت مساجد المحلة، ويحرر ومقتضى إطلاقهم أنها سنة كفاية أن المراد أنها سنة كفاية البلد لا في المحلة قوله فالصحيح أنه نال إحدى الفضيلتين) هما صلاتها في البيت جماعة، وصلاتها في المسجد جماعة. قوله: (فإن الأداء الخ) علة لمحذوف كان الواجب ذكره، وهو الأفضل فيها المسجد فإنّ الأداء الخ. قال البرهان الحلبي كل ما شرع بجماعة فالمسجد فيه أفضل لزيادة فضيلة المسجد، وتكثير الجماعة، وإظهار شعار الإسلام اهـ وفي النهر أنها في المسجد أفضل على ما عليه الاعتماد. قوله: (ووقتها ما بعد صلاة العشاء) أي الوقت الذي هو بعد صلاة العشاء قوله : يصح تقديم الوتر على التراويح الخ) وقيل وقتها بعد العشاء قيل الوتر وبه قال عامة مشايخ بخارى، وأثر الخلاف يظهر فيما لو فاتته ترويحة لو اشتغل بها يفوته الوتر بالجماعة يشتغل بالترويحة على قول مشایخ بخاری وبالوتر على قول غيرهم. قوله : (وقال جماعة من أصحابنا الخ) قال في البحر، ولم أر من صححه، وإذا فاتت قيل: تقضي ما لم يأت وقتها من الليلة المستقبلة، وقيل: ما لم يمض الشهر، والصحيح أنها لا تقضى مطلقاً فإن قضاها كانت نفلاً لا تراويح كما والسراج قوله : ( وقال بعضهم : لا يكره الخ أي تحريماً، وإلا فمخالفة الأولى ثابتة بدليل في الدر،
And its time: after the Isha prayer, according to the correct view, until dawn. And due to its following Isha, it is valid to offer Witr before Tarawih and to delay it after, and the latter is better. So much so that if it becomes clear that the Isha prayer was invalid while Tarawih and Witr were valid, they repeat Isha and then Tarawih but not Witr according to Abu Hanifah, because it (Witr) falls as an absolute supererogatory prayer due to its being in an improper place. That is the correct view. Some of our companions, among them Isma'il al-Zahid, said that the entire night is its time, before Isha and after it, before Witr and after it, because it is qiyam al-layl. It is recommended to delay Tarawih until near the last third of the night or near its half. They differed about performing it after the half: some said it is makruh because it follows Isha and thus becomes like the sunnah of Isha; others said it is not makruh to delay it... (then comments on the hadith about the number of rak'ahs, and discussions about congregation being sunnah kifayah, and the best place for prayer). His statement: 'And its time is after Isha prayer' means the time that is after Isha prayer. His statement: 'It is valid to offer Witr before Tarawih, etc.' It is also said that its time is after Isha and after Witr, and this is the view of generally all the mashayikh of Bukhara. The effect of the difference appears in the case where one misses a tarwiha: if he occupies himself with it and misses Witr in congregation, he should occupy himself with the tarwiha according to the mashayikh of Bukhara, and with Witr according to others. His statement: 'And a group of our companions, among them Isma'il al-Zahid...' al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone who corrected it. If it is missed, it is said: one makes it up as long as its time of the coming night has not come; it is said: as long as the month has not passed; the correct view is that it is not made up at all, and if one does make it up, it is nafl, not Tarawih. His statement: 'And some said: it is not makruh...' meaning not makruh tahrimi, otherwise going against the better is established by evidence.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage refines the rulings regarding the time of Tarawih. The correct position is that Tarawih is prayed after the Isha prayer, extending until dawn. Because Tarawih follows Isha, it is permissible to pray Witr before Tarawih, but delaying Witr until after Tarawih is better. If Isha is later found invalid, one repeats Isha and Tarawih but not Witr, according to Abu Hanifah, because Witr becomes an absolute nafl. Some Hanafi scholars, like Isma'il al-Zahid, hold that the entire night is valid for Tarawih, as it is qiyam al-layl. It is recommended to delay Tarawih to the last third or halfway through the night. There is disagreement about praying it after the half: some consider it makruh (disliked) due to it becoming like the sunnah of Isha, while others do not. The passage also includes discussions about the number of rak'ahs and the virtue of congregation. It further addresses the issue of making up missed Tarawih: the correct view is that they are not made up; if one does, they count as nafl, not Tarawih.

Key Terms
وقت (waqt): The prescribed time for Tarawih: from after Isha until dawn.
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayers, which is wajib in the Hanafi school.
قيام الليل (qiyam al-layl): Night vigil prayer; the minority view uses this to extend Tarawih time to the entire night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It must be made up before the next night
B) It may be made up within the month
C) It is not made up at all; if done, it counts as nafl
D) It is made up after Ramadan

Key Takeaway
Tarawih time is after Isha; Witr after Tarawih is better; missed Tarawih is not made up.

Taraweeh Congregation: Sunna Kifaya and Its Proof
Ruling on communal aspect of Taraweeh and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Taraweeh congregation and explain the evidence from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
Taraweeh in congregation is a communal sunna (sunna kifaya), not an individual obligation.

The source clarifies a common confusion: Is Taraweeh congregation required for every individual? The Hanafi school teaches that it is a sunna kifaya, meaning if some people in a locality perform it in congregation, the rest are absolved. The proof comes from the actions of prominent Companions like Ibn Umar, who sometimes prayed at home.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that congregation in Taraweeh is a sunna kifaya. Identify the act (congregation) and its ruling level (sunna kifaya, a type of sunna muakkada).
Sunna kifaya is a communal recommended act.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the practice of Ibn Umar, Urwa, Salim, al-Qasim, Ibrahim, and Nafi' who prayed Taraweeh individually at home. This is a Qawl Sahabi (action of a Companion) used as proof.
The dalil is textual: they did it, so it is permissible.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
If congregation were an individual obligation (fard ayn), these Companions would not have abandoned it. Since they did, it proves the ruling is not obligatory on each person.
The reasoning: impossibility of them abandoning a sunna muakkada if it were ayn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text indicates no disagreement among Hanafi authorities; it is muttafaq alayh. However, the scope (locality vs. town) is clarified.
The ikhtilaf is about the scope, not the ruling itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that congregation in the mosque is superior to congregation at home, as affirmed by al-Burhan al-Halabi and al-Nahr.
The mosque is preferred for its added virtues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصدر الشهيد الجماعة سنة كفاية فيها حتى لو أقامها البعض في المسجد بجماعة وباقي أهل المحلة أقامها منفرداً في بيته لا يكون تاركاً للسنة لأنه يروى عن أفراد الصحابة التخلف، وقال في المبسوط : لو صلي إنسان في بيته لا يأثم فقد فعله ابن عمر وعروة، وسالم والقاسم وابراهيم، ونافع فدل فعل هؤلاء أن الجماعة في المسجد سنة على سبيل الكفاية إذ لا يظن بابن عمر ومن تبعه ترك السنة انتهى وإن صلاها بجماعة في بيته فالصحيح أنه نال إحدى الفضيلتين فإن الأداء في المسجد له فضيلة ليس للأداء في البيت ذلك وكذا الحكم في الفرائض. قوله: (وباقي أهل المحلة أقامها منفرداً أفاد بهذا التعبير أنها سنة كفاية لكل محلة فيها مسجد فإقامتها بمسجد واحد في البلد لا تسقط الجماعة عن جميعهم حيث تعددت مساجد المحلة، ويحرر ومقتضى إطلاقهم أنها سنة كفاية أن المراد أنها سنة كفاية البلد لا في المحلة قوله فالصحيح أنه نال إحدى الفضيلتين) هما صلاتها في البيت جماعة، وصلاتها في المسجد جماعة. قوله: (فإن الأداء الخ) علة لمحذوف كان الواجب ذكره، وهو الأفضل فيها المسجد فإنّ الأداء الخ. قال البرهان الحلبي كل ما شرع بجماعة فالمسجد فيه أفضل لزيادة فضيلة المسجد، وتكثير الجماعة، وإظهار شعار الإسلام اهـ وفي النهر أنها في المسجد أفضل على ما عليه الاعتماد.
The imam al-sadr al-shahid said: Congregation in Taraweeh is a sunna kifaya, such that even if some people perform it in congregation in the mosque and the rest of the inhabitants of the locality pray it individually in their houses, they are not abandoners of the sunna because it is narrated that some individuals among the Companions used to stay behind. And it is said in al-Mabsut: If a person prays in his house, he does not sin; indeed Ibn Umar, Urwa, Salim, al-Qasim, Ibrahim, and Nafi' did that. So the action of these people indicates that congregation in the mosque is a sunna on the basis of sufficiency, for it cannot be assumed that Ibn Umar and those who followed him would abandon the sunna. End. And if he prays it in congregation in his house, the correct view is that he attains one of the two virtues, for performing it in the mosque has a virtue that performance at home does not. And the same applies to the obligatory prayers. He said: (And the rest of the inhabitants of the locality pray it individually) This expression indicates that it is a sunna kifaya for every locality that has a mosque; performing it in one mosque in the town does not remove the obligation of congregation from all of them if there are multiple mosques in the locality. And it is reviewed: The implication of their absolute statement that it is a sunna kifaya is that it is a sunna kifaya for the town, not for the locality. He said: (The correct view is that he attains one of the two virtues) They are: praying it in congregation at home, and praying it in congregation in the mosque. He said: (Indeed performing it in the mosque has a virtue) is the cause for something omitted that should have been mentioned, which is that the mosque is more virtuous. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: Every act of worship legislated in congregation, the mosque is more virtuous for it due to the added virtue of the mosque, the greater number of the congregation, and the manifesting of the symbols of Islam. End. And in al-Nahr: It is more virtuous in the mosque, and that is the relied-upon position.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that Taraweeh prayer in congregation is a communal sunna (sunna kifaya). The matn begins by citing the authoritative view (al-sadr al-shahid) that it is not an individual obligation. The evidence comes from the practice of several Companions, including Ibn Umar, who occasionally prayed Taraweeh at home alone. Al-Mabsut, a core Zahir al-Riwayah text, confirms that such individual prayer is not sinful, and that the congregation in the mosque is a sunna kifaya. The hashiya then clarifies the scope: if there are multiple mosques in a locality, the sunna is fulfilled only if each locality holds a congregation; a single mosque congregation does not suffice for all. The commentary further explains that praying in congregation at home grants one virtue, but the mosque is superior. Al-Burhan al-Halabi and al-Nahr affirm the preference for the mosque due to additional benefits like manifesting Islamic symbols and increasing the congregation. This ruling applies similarly to obligatory prayers (fara'id).

Key Terms
سنة كفاية (sunna kifaya): A recommended act that is sufficient for the community to perform; if some fulfill it, the rest are absolved of blame.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed with an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person prays Taraweeh individually at home, what is the ruling?
A) He commits a sin.
B) He does not sin, but loses the virtue of congregation.
C) He attains the same virtue as congregational prayer.
D) His prayer is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Taraweeh congregation is sunna kifaya: not wajib on every individual, but communal; the mosque remains the most virtuous place.

Time of Taraweeh and Its Sequence with Witr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on time and sequence rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi time for Taraweeh, explain the dispute about delaying it after half the night, and apply the ruling on sequence with Witr.

Core Idea
Taraweeh time is after Isha until Fajr; delaying beyond half the night is better avoided.

This lesson focuses on the time window for Taraweeh prayer and its relationship with Witr. We explore the correct view that restricts Taraweeh to after Isha, the minority view that it can be prayed throughout the night, and the practical differences this creates. You will learn how the subsidiary status of Taraweeh to Isha drives the ruling and why the preferred position is to perform Witr first and not delay Taraweeh excessively.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (Taraweeh) and the primary ruling on its time: after Isha until Fajr. Note this is the 'correct' (as-sahih) view.
The matn explicitly states 'after Isha prayer on the correct view until dawn'.
2
Analyze the subsidiary link to Isha
Understand why Taraweeh is tied to Isha: it is subsidiary (tabi') to Isha. This link affects the sequence with Witr and the consequences if Isha is invalid.
The phrase 'due to its being subsidiary to Isha' is key.
3
Examine the sequence with Witr
State that it is valid to pray Witr before or after Taraweeh, but Witr first is better. Apply the hypothetical of invalid Isha: Witr is not repeated because it becomes absolute nafl.
The hypothetical shows the subsidiary relationship in action.
4
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on time scope
Contrast the correct view (after Isha only) with the minority view (all night) from Isma'il al-Zahid. Note the reasoning: Taraweeh is qiyam al-layl. Assess the authority of the minority view.
Al-Bahr comments: 'I haven't seen anyone who deemed it correct.'
5
Resolve the delay after half the night
Differentiate between the recommended delay (until before third/half) and the disagreement on performing after half. Identify the preferred view: not to delay, even if not strictly makruh.
The hashiya stresses that it is more beloved not to delay, fearing missing the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(And its time) is after the Isha prayer, correct view, until dawn. (And) due to its being subsidiary to Isha, (it is valid to perform Witr before Taraweeh and to delay it after it, and the [Witr] is better. Even if it becomes clear that Isha was invalid but Taraweeh and Witr were not, they would repeat Isha then Taraweeh but not Witr according to Abu Hanifa because it falls as an absolute nafl due to being outside its proper time; this is the correct view. And a group of our companions, including Isma'il al-Zahid, said that the entire night is its time, before Isha and after it, and before Witr and after it, because it is qiyam al-layl. (And it is recommended to delay Taraweeh to shortly before the last third of the night or shortly before its half. And they differed about performing it after the half: some said it is disliked because it is subsidiary to Isha, so it becomes like the sunna of Isha; and some said it is not disliked to delay it. He said: But it is more beloved not to delay Taraweeh. He said: (its end) can be read in the nominative, with an omitted genitive, i.e., the prayer of its end, or in the accusative as an adverb, i.e., the prayer occurring at its end. He said: (in its own right) i.e., not with respect to Taraweeh. He said: (and its time is after Isha) i.e., the time that is after Isha. He said: (it is valid to present Witr before Taraweeh, etc.) And it is said its time is after Isha before Witr, and that was the view of most mashayikh of Bukhara. The effect of the difference appears in the case where one misses a tarwiha: if he occupies himself with it, he would miss Witr in congregation; he should occupy himself with the tarwiha according to the mashayikh of Bukhara, and with Witr according to others. He said: (and a group of our companions, etc.) He said in al-Bahr: I haven't seen anyone who deemed it correct. And if it is missed, it is said: make it up as long as its time of the following night has not come; and it is said: as long as the month has not ended; and the correct view is that it is not made up at all, and if one makes it up it becomes nafl, not Taraweeh. He said: (and some said it is not disliked) i.e., not prohibitedly disliked, but going against the better is established by evidence. (to its after) i.e., after half the night, the correct view, because the best part of the night prayer is its end in its own right, but it is more beloved not to delay Taraweeh to that time for fear of missing it.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage addresses the time of Taraweeh and its sequence with Witr. The matn states the correct view that its time is after Isha until Fajr. Since Taraweeh is subsidiary to Isha, it is valid to pray Witr before it or after, but performing Witr first is better. A hypothetical: if Isha turns out invalid, Witr is not repeated because it becomes absolute nafl when offered outside its proper time. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: a group (including Isma'il al-Zahid) holds that the entire night (before Isha, after Isha, before or after Witr) is valid time, reasoning that Taraweeh is qiyam al-layl. The matn also recommends delaying Taraweeh until near the last third or half of the night, but there is disagreement on performing it after half: some consider it makruh because it follows Isha like its sunna; others say no karaha. The hashiya clarifies that the preferred view is not to delay it after half, even though the end of the night is virtuous for night prayer, due to fear of missing the prayer altogether. The commentary further discusses differences among mashayikh of Bukhara about priority when one cannot attend both Taraweeh and Witr in congregation.

Key Terms
وقت التراويح (waqt al-taraweeh): The time for Taraweeh prayer: after Isha until Fajr (correct view).
قيام الليل (qiyam al-layl): Night prayer; used as reasoning by some to allow Taraweeh at any part of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram
B) It is makruh tahrimi according to all
C) The preferred view is not to delay, but it is not prohibited
D) It is mustahab

Key Takeaway
Taraweeh should be performed after Isha until Fajr, and while delaying to the last third is recommended, delaying past half the night is better avoided.

Taraweeh: 20 Rak'ahs and the Ruling on Sitting After Pairs
Establishing 20 rak'ahs for Taraweeh and rules for sitting after pairs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of rak'ahs in Taraweeh, explain the ruling on sitting after every two rak'ahs, and identify the proof from the consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
Taraweeh is 20 rak'ahs with taslim after every two; sitting after each pair is makruh but valid.

This lesson examines the established number of rak'ahs in Taraweeh prayer and the rulings concerning when one sits after the pairs. The text, from a Hanafi commentary, affirms the 20-rak'ah count by consensus and clarifies that sitting after every two is disliked yet the prayer remains valid. Understanding these details ensures one follows the sunna correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
The text explicitly states that Taraweeh is twenty rak'ahs, performed as ten taslims (each taslim is two rak'ahs).
This is the established Hanafi position, transmitted successively from the Companions.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is the consensus (ijma') of the Companions and the mutawatir (successive) practice. The text says 'by the consensus of the Companions' and 'as is transmitted successively.'
Ijma' is a definitive proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the ruling on sitting after pairs
If one intentionally sits after every two rak'ahs (i.e., rests between each pair), the most correct view is that it is makruh (disliked) but the prayer is valid and suffices.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference; the text declares al-asahh (most correct) as makruh.
4
Distinguish different sitting patterns
If one sits only after every four rak'ahs, that sitting counts as a taslim for two rak'ahs. If one does not sit at all except at the end of twenty, it only counts as two rak'ahs (not twenty).
This shows the importance of following the prescribed structure.
5
Apply the recommended practice
It is sunna to sit after every four rak'ahs for a rest equal to the prayer time, and also between the fifth tarwiha and Witr. During these rests, one may recite, pray individually, or remain silent.
The name 'taraweeh' is derived from these rests (tarwiha).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي عشرون ركعة) باجماع الله الصحابة رضي عنهم بعشر تسليمات) كما هو المتوارث يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين فإذا وصلها وجلس على كل شفع فالأصح أنه إن تعمد ذلك كره وصحت وأجزأته عن كلها وإذا لم يجلس إلا في آخر أربع نابت عن تسليمة فتكون بمنزلة ركعتين في الصحيح (ويستحب الجلوس بعد صلاة (كل) أربع ركعات بقدرها وكذا يستحب الجلوس بقدرها (بين الترويحة الخامسة والوتر) لأنه المتوارث عن السلف، وهذا روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ولأن اسم التراويح بني عن ذلك وهم مخيرون في الجلوس بين التسبيح والقراءة والصلاة فرادى، والسكوت. قوله: (وهي عشرون ركعة) الحكمة في تقديرها بهذا العدد مساواة المكمل وهي السنن للمكمل، وهي الفرائض الاعتقادية والعملية. قوله: (فالأصح أنه إن تعمد ذلك كره مقابله ما في منية المصلي من عدم الكراهة لأنه أكمل لزيادة المشقة ورد بأن الكمال لا يحصل بمجرد المشقة ما لم يكن فيه اتباع السنة .اهـ. قوله : (وإذا لم يجلس إلا في آخر أربع (الخ) أي آخر كل أربع فإذا جلس على آخر كل ركعتين تنوب عن تسليمتين على ما عليه العامة ذكره السيد، وإذا لم يقعد إلا في آخر العشرين فعلى الصحيح تجوز عن تسليمة أي ركعتين بخلاف ما إذا قعد على رأس ركعتين كما في الخلاصة. قوله: (نابت عن تسليمة فيه أنهم قالوا: إن القعود الأوّل في رباعية النفل واجب يجبر بالسجود، ومقتضاه أن تنوب عن تسليمتين ويجب عليه السجود إن كان ساهياً، وقد يجاب بأن المذكور هنا في خصوص التراويح لكونها شرعت على هيئة مخصوصة بالسلام على رأس الركعتين، فلا ينافي أنها في غيرها تجعل أربعاً، وفيه أن هذا يرد على ما إذا جمع الكل بتسليمة واحدة مع أنها إنما تنوب عن تسليمة واحدة على المفتي به كما في الدر. قوله: (والصلاة فرادي) أي بعد كل أربع أما بعد كل شفع فهي مكروهة. قال البرهان الحلبي : يكره صلاة ركعتين منفرداً بعد كل ركعتين لأنها بدعة مخالفة مع الإمام اهـ، وفي الكافي وتكره الإستراحة على خمس تسليمات عند الجمهور.
It is twenty rak'ahs, by the consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, with ten taslims, as is transmitted successively. One makes taslim after every two rak'ahs. If he joins them and sits at every pair, the most correct is that if he does so intentionally, it is disliked but valid and suffices for all. And if he does not sit except at the end of four, it stands for a taslim, and it is regarded as two rak'ahs, according to the correct view. (And it is recommended to sit after every four rak'ahs for the duration of four, and likewise it is recommended to sit for that duration between the fifth tarwiha and Witr, because it is transmitted from the predecessors, and this is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and because the name 'taraweeh' is derived from that. And they have a choice in sitting between tasbih, recitation, praying individually, and silence. He said: (It is twenty rak'ahs) The wisdom in fixing this number is to equalize the supplement (sunan) to the supplemented (the obligatory acts of belief and practice). He said: (If he does so intentionally, it is disliked) The opposite view in Muniya al-Musalli says no karaha because it is more complete due to increased hardship, but this is refuted because completeness is not achieved by mere hardship without following the sunna. End. He said: (And if he does not sit except at the end of four) i.e., the end of every four; if he sits at the end of every two, it stands for two taslims according to the general view, as mentioned by al-Sayyid. And if he does not sit except at the end of the twenty, then the correct view is that it suffices for one taslim, i.e., two rak'ahs, unlike the case when he sits at the end of two, as in al-Khulasa. He said: (It stands for a taslim) There is an implication that they said: The first sitting in a four-rak'ah nafl is wajib and compensated by sajda; accordingly it should stand for two taslims and sajda is required if he forgot. It may be answered that what is mentioned here is specific to Taraweeh because it is legislated in a specific manner with taslim after every two, and this does not contradict that in other prayers it is made four. There is also a point that this refutes the case when one combines all with a single taslim, whereas it only suffices for one taslim according to the mufta bihi as in al-Durr. He said: (And praying individually) i.e., after every four; as for after every pair, it is disliked. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: It is disliked to pray two rak'ahs individually after every two, because it is a bid'a contrary to the imam. End. And in al-Kafi: Resting on five taslims is disliked according to the majority.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage firmly establishes that Taraweeh consists of 20 rak'ahs, based on the consensus of the Companions. The sunna method is to make taslim after every two rak'ahs, totaling ten taslims. If someone intentionally sits after every two rak'ahs (i.e., does not stand immediately for the next pair), this is disliked but the prayer is valid. The hashiya explains that if one sits only after every four rak'ahs, that counts as a taslim for two rak'ahs. The recommended practice is to sit after every four rak'ahs for a rest equal to the prayer duration, and similarly between the fifth tarwiha and Witr. This custom is traced to Abu Hanifa and the early Muslims. During these rests, one may engage in tasbih, recitation, solitary prayer, or silence. The hashiya then delves into fiqh details: if one performs all twenty with a single taslim (i.e., no sitting except at the end), it only counts as two rak'ahs. There is also discussion about whether the first sitting in a four-rak'ah nafl is wajib, but since Taraweeh is specifically legislated as two-rak'ah units, the rules differ. The commentary also prohibits praying two rak'ahs individually after every two rak'ahs (i.e., in addition to the established sunna), as it is a disliked innovation.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslima): A unit of two rak'ahs concluded with taslim; Taraweeh has ten such units.
الترويحة (al-tarwiha): A rest period after every four rak'ahs or between the fifth tarwiha and Witr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib
B) It is mustahab
C) It is makruh but valid
D) It invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
Taraweeh is 20 rak'ahs by consensus; making taslim after every two is sunna, but sitting after each pair is makruh yet valid.
