Khatm al-Qur'an in Taraweeh: Frequency and Ruling
Ruling on khatm frequency and imam replacement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Qur'an during Taraweeh and identify the recommended frequencies and trustee conditions for the imam.

Core Idea
Completing the Qur'an in Taraweeh is sunna once a month; more is better, but not obligatory.

Taraweeh is a special night prayer in Ramadan. One of its sunan is to complete a full recitation of the Qur'an over the month. This lesson explains the recommended frequency and what to do if the imam cannot complete the recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is completing the entire Qur'an (khatm) during Taraweeh prayers. The ruling is sunna (recommended), not wajib or fard.
Sunnah muakkadah in this context means highly recommended but not obligatory.
2
Note the Recommended Frequencies
The text states: once a month (the minimum sunna), twice is virtuous (fadilah), and three times (once every ten days) is better (afdal). This indicates that more is better.
The source 'al-Kafi' is cited for the three-time recommendation.
3
Handle the Imam's Inability or Mistakes
If the imam of a living mosque cannot complete a khatm, he may delegate to another imam. Similarly, if the imam is a lahan (makes frequent recitation mistakes), he may be replaced to ensure proper recitation.
This ensures the sunna is fulfilled even if the regular imam is not proficient.
4
Consider Completing Before Month's End
If the khatm is completed before the end of Ramadan, some scholars say it is not disliked to stop Taraweeh for the remaining nights, because Taraweeh is legislated for recitation. However, the text implies this is a minority view.
The main position is to continue Taraweeh with other recitation if khatm is done early.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وسن ختم القرآن فيها أي التراويح (مرة في الشهر على. قوله: (مرة في الشهر) ومرتين فضيلة، وثلاثاً في كل عشر مرة أفضل كافي، وإذا كان إمام مسجد حية لا يختم فله أن يتركه إلى غيره كما في الفتح، وكذا لو كان الإمام لحاناً، وفي الفتح، والتبيين، ثم إذا ختم مرة قبل آخره قيل : لا يكره وترك التراويح فيما بقي لأنها شرعت
(And it is sunna to complete the Qur'an in it, i.e., Taraweeh, once in the month) upon. He said: (Once in the month) and twice is a virtue, and three times (once every ten days) is better, as in al-Kafi. And if the imam of a living mosque does not complete it, he may leave it to someone else, as in al-Fath; similarly if the imam is a lahan (makes mistakes in recitation). And in al-Fath and al-Tabyin: Then if he completes once before the end of the month, it is said: it is not disliked and he may leave Taraweeh for the remaining days because it is legislated...
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage states that it is sunna to complete the entire Qur'an once during the Taraweeh prayers of Ramadan. The hashiya notes that completing it twice is virtuous, and three times (roughly once every ten days) is even better. If the imam is unable to complete a khatm, another person may take over. Similarly, if the imam is a lahan (makes many mistakes in recitation) he may be replaced. If the khatm is completed before the end of the month, some say it is not disliked to stop Taraweeh for the remaining nights, but this is a minority view. The text cuts off, but the ruling is clear: completing the Qur'an once is the minimum sunna.

Key Terms
ختم القرآن (khatm al-Qur'an): Complete recitation of the entire Qur'an from beginning to end during Taraweeh prayers.
لحان (lahhan): An imam who makes frequent mistakes in Quranic recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is wajib
B) It is sunna once in the month
C) It is mustahab to do it three times
D) It is not recommended

Key Takeaway
Completing the Qur'an in Taraweeh is sunna, not wajib; once is the minimum, more is better, and an imam who cannot complete or recites poorly may delegate.

Number of Tarawih Rak'ahs and Sitting Rulings
Explains the 20 rak'ah consensus and rulings on sitting between sets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of Tarawih rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school and explain the rulings on sitting between the rak'ah sets.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs by Companion consensus; sitting after every four is recommended, and sitting at every pair is disliked but valid.

This lesson clarifies the established number of Tarawih rak'ahs and the nuances of sitting during the prayer, based on the consensus of the Companions and the practice transmitted from the Salaf. Understanding these rulings helps avoid common misconceptions and correctly implement this emphasized sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling and its proof
Locate the explicit statement in the text: Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs by consensus of the Companions (bajmāʿ al-ṣaḥābah). Note that this is transmitted (mutawārith) and is the binding position.
This is the primary ruling—20 rak'ahs, not 8 or 36.
2
Understand the standard method of praying
The prayer is divided into ten taslims, each after two rak'ahs. This is the inherited practice.
Hanafi nafl is prayed in pairs; Tarawih is no exception.
3
Examine the ruling on sitting at every pair
If one prays all 20 rak'ahs without sitting except at the end, then deliberately sits at every two rak'ahs, it is disliked (makruh) but valid and suffices for all rak'ahs.
The dislikedness is for departing from the recommended pattern.
4
Analyze the alternative: sitting after every four
If one sits only after every four rak'ahs (i.e., after two pairs), that sitting substitutes for one taslim, and the four rak'ahs are considered like two rak'ahs in effect.
This is the more virtuous pattern.
5
Note the recommended sittings and options
It is recommended to sit after every four rak'ahs for the duration of those four, and also between the fifth tarwiha and witr. During these sittings, one may engage in tasbih, recitation, optional prayer, or silence.
The worshiper has flexibility; the sitting itself is a recommended break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي عشرون ركعة) باجماع الصحابة رضي الله عنهم بعشر تسليمات) كما هو المتوارث يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين فإذا وصلها وجلس على كل شفع فالأصح أنه إن تعمد ذلك كره وصحت وأجزأته عن كلها وإذا لم يجلس إلا في آخر أربع نابت عن تسليمة فتكون بمنزلة ركعتين في الصحيح (ويستحب الجلوس بعد صلاة (كل) أربع ركعات بقدرها وكذا يستحب الجلوس بقدرها (بين الترويحة الخامسة والوتر) لأنه المتوارث عن السلف، وهذا روي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ولأن اسم التراويح بني عن ذلك وهم مخيرون في الجلوس بين التسبيح والقراءة والصلاة فرادى، والسكوت
(It is twenty rak'ahs) by consensus of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, with ten taslims (salutations) as inherited, one says salaam at the end of every two rak'ahs. If he connects (all) and sits at every pair (salutes), the most correct (view) is that if he does so deliberately, it is disliked but valid and suffices for all [the rak'ahs]. If he does not sit except at the end of four, it substitutes for one taslim, so it is like two rak'ahs in the correct (view). (And it is recommended to sit after every four rak'ahs for the duration of them, and likewise it is recommended to sit for the duration between the fifth tarwiha and witr) because it is inherited from the predecessors, and this is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and because the name tarawih is built upon that. They are given a choice in sitting between tasbih, recitation, praying individually, and silence.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage establishes that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs based on the consensus of the Companions, transmitted from them. Each two rak'ahs ends with a taslim. The author discusses the ruling if one prays all twenty rak'ahs without sitting except at the end: the correct view is that it is disliked (makruh) if intentional, but valid, and it suffices for all rak'ahs. If one sits only after every four rak'ahs, that substitutes for one taslim, counting as two rak'ahs. It is recommended (mustahabb) to sit after every four rak'ahs for the duration of those four, and also between the fifth tarwiha and witr. This practice is inherited from the Salaf and reported from Abu Hanifa. The worshiper is free to use the sitting time for tasbih, recitation, optional prayer individually, or silence.

Key Terms
التسليمات (al-taslimāt): The number of times one says the salaam (ending the prayer); here meaning the number of two-rak'ah units.
الشفع (al-shaf‘): A pair, meaning here a set of two rak'ahs in Tarawih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 20
C) 36
D) 12

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is firmly established as 20 rak'ahs by ijma, and the recommended practice includes sitting after every four rak'ahs, not every two.

Recitation in Tarawih: Khatm and Avoiding Aversion
Sunnah of khatm, amount per rak'ah, and overriding aversion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah amount of Quran recitation in Tarawih per rak'ah and explain the overriding condition that prioritizes congregational attendance.

Core Idea
Complete the Quran once a month in Tarawih, but do not drive people away.

Tarawih prayer is a sunnah of Ramadan. One of its recommended practices is to complete the entire Quran (khatm) over the month, with roughly ten verses recited per rak'ah. However, the primary goal is to maintain congregation attendance. If lengthy recitation causes aversion, the imam should shorten it, even if that means not completing a full khatm. This lesson examines the evidence and the critical refinement that balances ideal recitation with practical congregational needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah ruling
The act is reciting Quran in Tarawih. The text states that completing the Quran once a month is sunnah (recommended). This is the baseline ruling.
Sunnah here means a consistent practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the early community.
2
Note the prescribed amount per rak'ah
The majority opinion, narrated from Abu Hanifa, is to recite ten verses or similar in each rak'ah. This provides a concrete guideline for the imam.
Ten verses is an average; the exact amount can vary but should not be less than a meaningful portion.
3
Recognize the overriding condition: aversion of the congregation
If completing the full khatm (or reciting ten verses) causes the congregation to become averse or leave, the imam must shorten the recitation. The condition of not causing aversion takes precedence over completing the khatm.
Aversion is judged by the local congregation's tolerance; the imam should observe and adjust.
4
Understand the mufta bihi: short surahs to encourage attendance
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to recite short surahs from al-Mufassal (the last section of the Quran), similar to Maghrib prayer. This keeps the recitation brief and attractive, maintaining congregation numbers.
Al-Zahidi's opinion is cited: recite as in Maghrib (short surahs after Fatiha).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسن ختم القرآن فيها أي التراويح (مرة في الشهر على الصحيح) وهو قول الأكثر رواه الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات، أو نحوها وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه كان يختم في رمضان إحدى وستين ختمة ختمة، وفي كل ليلة ختمة، وفي كل التراويح ختمة وصلى بالقرآن في ركعتين وإن مل به أي بختم القرآن في الشهر (القوم قرأ بقدر ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفيرهم في المختار) لأن الأفضل في زماننا ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير الجماعة كذا في الاختيار، وفي المحيط الأفضل في زماننا أن يقرأ بما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير القوم عن الجماعة لأنّ تكثير القوم أفضل من تطويل القراءة، وبه يفتى، وقال الزاهدي: يقرأ كما في المغرب أي بقصار المفصل بعد الفاتحة
(And it is sunnah to complete the Quran in it, i.e. Tarawih, once a month on the correct view) and it is the opinion of the majority, narrated from al-Hasan on the authority of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: that one recites ten verses or similar in each rak'ah. And from Abu Hanifa that he used to complete (the Quran) sixty-one times in Ramadan: once each night, and once in all the Tarawih, and he prayed with the Quran in two rak'ahs every day. (And if the people are averse to completing the Quran in a month, he recites as much as does not cause aversion, in al-Mukhtar) because the best in our time is that which does not cause aversion to the congregation. Similarly in al-Ikhtiyar, and in al-Muhit: the best in our time is to recite what does not cause aversion to the congregation, for increasing the number of people is better than lengthening the recitation, and that is the fatwa. Al-Zahidi said: He recites as in Maghrib i.e. the short surahs of al-Mufassal after al-Fatiha.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended recitation in Tarawih. The sunnah is to complete the entire Quran once in the month, as narrated from Abu Hanifa. The typical amount is about ten verses per rak'ah. However, if the congregation becomes averse due to the length, the imam should shorten the recitation to avoid driving them away. The preferred practice in our time is to recite in a manner that does not cause aversion, as increasing the number of worshippers is more virtuous than lengthy recitation. Al-Zahidi's opinion suggests reciting short surahs of al-Mufassal from the Maghrib section, meaning medium or short surahs after Fatiha.

Key Terms
الختم (al-khatm): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran.
المفصل (al-mufaṣṣal): The last section of the Quran (from Qaf or al-Hujurat to the end), divided into long, medium, and short. 'Qisar al-mufassal' are the shortest surahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the congregation is averse to the imam completing the Quran in Tarawih?
A) He must still complete it.
B) He should recite in a way that does not cause aversion.
C) He should stop Tarawih.
D) He should recite even longer to increase reward.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of completing the Quran in Tarawih is commendable, but it is subordinate to the greater good of maintaining the congregation; therefore, the imam should recite short surahs if needed.

Disliked Recitation and Obligation of Salat on Prophet
States two rulings on recitation and salat in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disliked amount of recitation after al-Fatiha and explain the Hanafi position on sending blessings in tashahhud.

Core Idea
Reciting less than three verses after Fatiha is prohibitively disliked; sending blessings on the Prophet in tashahhud is a stressed sunnah, not wajib but not to be omitted.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two important rulings for Tarawih prayer (and generally). First, it explains the minimum recitation after al-Fatiha that avoids dislike. Second, it addresses the status of the salat (blessings) on the Prophet in the tashahhud, highlighting a difference between the Hanafi school and other mujtahids. Understanding these rulings ensures your prayer is performed correctly and in accordance with the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on two acts: (1) reciting fewer than three short verses or one long verse after al-Fatiha in Tarawih, and (2) omitting the salat on the Prophet in the tashahhud. For (1), the ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
2
Locate the proof for the dislike
The dislikedness is due to 'abandoning the wajib' – the Hanafi school holds that reciting a surah or three verses after al-Fatiha is wajib in every rak'ah. Thus, falling short abandons an obligation.
The proof is implicit: the wajib nature of the recitation is derived from the Sunnah and Hanafi usul.
3
Identify the Hanafi position on salat on the Prophet
According to the Hanafis, sending blessings on the Prophet in the tashahhud is sunnah mu'akkada (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. The passage states this clearly: 'because it is an emphasized sunnah according to us.'
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some mujtahids (scholars from other schools) consider the salat on the Prophet to be obligatory (fard) in the tashahhud. The passage warns that the prayer is 'not valid without it' according to their view.
This ikhtilaf is a matter of legitimate ijtihad.
5
Determine the practical implication
Even though the Hanafi ruling is that salat is sunnah mu'akkada, the passage instructs: 'the prayer on the Prophet... is not to be abandoned' – because of the strong recommendation and to avoid any disagreement that could render the prayer invalid.
Thus, a Hanafi should always include it in every tashahhud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره الاقتصار على ما دون ثلاث آيات، أو آية طويلة بعد الفاتحة لترك الواجب ولا يترك الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في كل تشهد منها لأنها سنة مؤكدة عندنا، وفرض على قول بعض المجتهدين، فلا يصح بدونها
(And it is disliked to confine oneself to less than three verses, or one long verse after al-Fatiha, because it abandons the obligatory. And the prayer (Salat) on the Prophet, peace be upon him, is not to be abandoned in every tashahhud thereof (i.e., of Tarawih), because it is an emphasized sunnah according to us (the Hanafis), and obligatory according to some mujtahids, so the prayer is not valid without it.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage addresses two additional rulings. First, in Tarawih (and generally in prayer), it is makruh (disliked) to recite only one or two verses or one long verse after al-Fatiha, because that would be abandoning the wajib amount. The wajib is to recite at least three short verses or one long verse equivalent. Second, the tashahhud should include the salat (blessings) on the Prophet. In the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah mu'akkada and not wajib, but many scholars said it is a condition (fard) outside the school. Therefore, to be safe, one should never omit it, as the prayer may be considered invalid according to some.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of at-tahiyyat in the sitting of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Reciting only one long verse
C) Reciting a long surah
D) Reciting with a loud voice

Key Takeaway
Reciting fewer than three verses after al-Fatiha is makruh tahrimi, and sending blessings on the Prophet in tashahhud is a sunnah mu'akkada that should never be omitted.

Rulings on Recitation, Sunan, and Qada of Tarawih
Commentary on Tarawih rulings with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum recitation in Tarawih, explain why omission is makruh tahrimi, and apply the rule that missed Tarawih is not qada but nafl.

Core Idea
Tarawih recitation below two short verses is makruh tahrimi; missing it cannot be made up as Tarawih.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies critical rulings about Tarawih prayer: how much Quran must be recited, what happens if the congregation is bored, and whether Tarawih can be made up later. We'll unpack the proofs and the Hanafi position on these issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage discusses three acts: recitation in each rak'ah of Tarawih, sending salawat in tashahhud, and the status of Tarawih after its time. Determine the hukm level of each.
Recitation: at least three short verses is wajib; omission is makruh tahrimi. Salawat: sunnah mu'akkada. Qada: not done.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof for shortening recitation when the congregation is bored. The passage mentions a hadith of the Prophet (saw) prohibiting Ubayy from lengthening recitation.
Also note the principle: increasing congregation size is better than lengthening recitation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The prohibition (nahy) indicates that excessively long recitation is discouraged. Istihsan prioritizes keeping the congregation over prolonging recitation.
The term 'al-mukhtar' shows this is the relied-upon view.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions a dispute over salawat: Hanafi holds it is sunnah mu'akkada, Shafi'i considers it fard. Also an intra-Hanafi difference on whether reciting only one or two verses is permissible without dislike.
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): validity of prayer differs between schools.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the operative ruling for fatwa: reciting at least three short verses after Fatiha is required; salawat is sunnah but not fard; missed Tarawih is not made up but can be prayed as nafl.
The tarjih authority is Al-Tahtawi, who follows the majority and criticizes the lenient view as weak.

Source Text

الصحيح) وهو قول الأكثر رواه الحسن على أبي حنيفة رحمه الله يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات، أو نحوها وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه كان يختم في رمضان إحدى وستين ختمة ختمة، وفي كل ليلة ختمة، وفي كل التراويح ختمة وصلى بالقرآن في ركعتين كل يوم في وصلى الفجر بوضوء العشاء أربعين سنة وإن مل به أي بختم القرآن في الشهر (القوم قرأ بقدر ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفيرهم في المختار) لأن الأفضل في زماننا ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير أفضل من تطويل القراءة) أي أكثر ثواباً لأنه يزاد بكل فرد صلاة، ويتعلم جاهلهم من عالمهم وتعود بركة الكامل منهم على التناقص. قوله : ( ويكره الإقتصار على ما دون ثلاث آيات، وآية طويلة بعد الفاتحة) أو آيتان متوسطتان كما في الشرح قوله لترك الواجب أفاد به أنه مكروه تحريماً، وما في فضائل رمضان للزاهدي من أنّ أبا الفضل الكرماني والوبري أفتيا أنه إذا قرأ في التراويح الفاتحة، وآية، أو آيتين لا يكره ومن لم يكن عالماً بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل انتهى محمول على الآية الطويلة، والآيتين المتوسطتين، أو هو ضعيف لأنّ فيه إفراطاً يؤدي إلى التفريط بترك الواجب قوله: (ولا) بترك الصلاة على النبي ( ويكتفي باللهم صل على محمد لأنه الفرض عند الشافعي [؟] . قوله : وفرض على قول بعض المجتهدين منهم مولانا الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه. ويحذر من الهدرمة، وترك الترتيل وترك تعديل الأركان وغيرها كما يفعله من له (ولو مل القوم) بذلك على المختار) لأنه عين الكسل منهم فلا يلتفت إليهم فيه (و) كذا (لا يترك الثناء) في افتتاح كل شفع (و) كذا تسبيح الركوع والسجود) لا يترك لافتراضه عند البعض، وتأكيد سنيته عندنا ولا يأتي الإمام (بالدعاء) عند السلام (إن مل القوم) به ولا يتركه بالمرة فيدعو بما قصر تحصيلاً للسنة ولا تقضى التراويح أصلاً (بفواتها) عن وقتها (منفرداً ولا بجماعة على الأصح لأنّ القضاء من خصائص الواجبات وإن قضاها كانت نفلاً مستحباً لا تراويح وهي سنة الوقت لا سنة الصوم في الأصح فمن صار أهلاً للصلاة في آخر اليوم يسن له التراويح كالحائض إذا طهرت والمسافر، والمريض المفطر . قوله : ( ويحذر من الهدرمة الموجود في النسخ التي بأيدينا بالدال المهملة والذي في الدر بالذال المعجمة، وفسرها في القاموس بسرعة الكلام والقراءة قوله : (وترك الترتيل) في القاموس رتل الكلام ترتيلاً، أحسن تأليفه اهـ والمراد أن لا يعطي التلاوة وحقها. قوله: (وغيرها) كترك التعوذ والتسمية، وترك الإستراحة فيما بين كل ترويحتين، والكراهة في الثلاثة المذكورة في كلامه تحريمية وفي غيرها تنزيهية لأنها في مقابلة ترك السنن . قوله : (وكذا لا يترك الثناء) سواء كان إماماً، أو مقتدياً، أو منفرداً وعلله في الفتح بأن السنن لا تترك للجماعات. قوله: (لافتراضه عند البعض هو أبو مطيع البلخي تلميذ الإمام الأعظم رضي الله عنه، وقيل بوجوبه قوله : (ولا) يأتي الإمام بالدعاء) أي الدعاء الطويل لقوله فيدعو بما قصر . قوله : (ولا تقضى التراويح لأنها ليست آكد من سنة المغرب والعشاء وهما لا يقضيان فهي أولى بعدم القضاء. قوله : (على الأصح) فقد تقدم مقابله . قوله : (والمسافر والمريض) لا يحسن عطفهما على الحائض لأنهما أهل لها قبل آخر اليوم وعبارته في الشرح أولى حيث قال : والأصح أنها سنة الوقت لقوله : وستنت لكم قيام ليله حتى أن المريض المفطر، والمسافر والحائض والنفساء إذا طهرتا والكافر إذا أسلم في آخر اليوم تسن لهم التراويح فكيف يعذر المقيم الصحيح الصائم في تركها اهـ وفي القنية لو تركوا الجماعة في الفرض ليس لهم أن يصلوا التراويح جماعة لأنها تبع له ولو لم يصلها بإمام له أن يصلي الوتر به كما أن له أن يصلي التراويح بإمام والوتر بآخر على الصحيح، ويكره للمقتدي أن يقعد في التراويح فإذا أراد الإمام أن يركع يقوم، وظاهر عبارة الشرح يفيد ثبوت الكراهة ولو كان داخلاً في صلاة الإمام لأنه علله بقوله لما في هذا من مخالفة الإمام، ولما فيه من القول بلزوم القيام في التراويح، وتكره مع غلبة النوم فينصرف حتى يستيقظ لأن في الصلاة مع النوم تهاوناً، وغفلة وترك التدبر ولا خصوصية لها بهذا بل كل الصلوات كذلك اهـ والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
The Book of Salah. The correct view, which is the opinion of the majority, narrated from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him: he recites in every rak'ah ten verses or approximately that. And from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he would complete the Qur'an in Ramadan sixty-one complete recitations: a complete recitation each night, and a complete recitation in all the Tarawih prayers. He prayed the whole Qur'an in two rak'ahs each day, and he prayed Fajr with the wudu of Isha for forty years. And if the people become bored with it (i.e., completing the Qur'an in the month), he recites according to what does not lead to their aversion (al-mukhtar). Because the best in our time is what does not lead to aversion of the congregation. Thus in al-Ikhtiyar, and in al-Muhit: the best in our time is to recite what does not lead to aversion of the people from the congregation, because increasing the people is better than lengthening the recitation, and according to this the fatwa is given. Al-Zahidi said: he recites as in Maghrib, i.e., short surahs of al-Mufassal after al-Fatihah. And it is disliked (makruh) to restrict to less than three verses, or a long verse after al-Fatihah, because it abandons the obligatory. And he should not abandon the salat upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in every tashahhud of it, because it is an emphatic sunnah according to us, and obligatory according to the statement of some mujtahids; so the prayer is not valid without it. For the sake of completing the Qur'an, and it has happened once. And it is said: he prays it, or recites whatever he wishes. And if he recites with completion and makes a mistake by leaving a surah or a verse and recites what comes after, it is recommended for him to recite the omitted then the recited, so as to be in order. His saying (he recites in every rak'ah ten verses or approximately that) because the number of rak'ahs of Tarawih is six hundred, or less by twenty if the month is incomplete, so he should increase more than ten if it is complete, because the verses exceed its measure completely by six hundred and sixty verses so that he may complete it. And all the verses of the Qur'an are six thousand, six hundred and sixty-six verses: one thousand of promise, one thousand of threat, one thousand of command, one thousand of prohibition, one thousand of stories, one thousand of news, five hundred of halal and haram, one hundred of supplication and glorification, and sixty-six of abrogating and abrogated. Thus in al-Sha'bi from al-Kashshaf. His saying (what does not lead to aversion of the congregation) from length of recitation, glorification, and supplications of tashahhud. And his statement 'in our time' has no significance, because the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, prohibited Ubayy from lengthening the recitation. His saying (because increasing the people is better than lengthening the recitation) i.e., more reward, because with each individual the prayer is increased, and their ignorant one learns from their knowledgeable one, and the blessing of the complete among them returns to the deficient. His saying (and it is disliked to restrict to less than three verses, and a long verse after al-Fatihah) or two medium verses, as in the Sharh. His saying 'because it abandons the obligatory' indicates that it is makruh tahrimi. And what is in Fada'il Ramadan of al-Zahidi from Abu al-Fadl al-Kirmani and al-Wabari that they gave a fatwa that if one recites in Tarawih al-Fatihah and one verse or two, it is not disliked, and whoever is not knowledgeable of the people of his time is ignorant—this is interpreted as the long verse and two medium verses, or it is weak because it involves excess leading to deficiency by abandoning the obligatory. His saying (and do not) by leaving the salat upon the Prophet, and he suffices with 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' because it is the obligatory according to al-Shafi'i [?]. His saying: it is obligatory according to some mujtahids, among them our master Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him. And he should beware of hasty recitation, leaving tarteel, and leaving straightening of the pillars, and other things, as does the one who (even if the people are bored with that, according to al-mukhtar) because it is pure laziness from them, so no attention is paid to them. Similarly, he should not leave the praise (thana') in the opening of every shaf' (pair), and similarly the glorification of ruku' and sujud, because some consider it obligatory, while according to us its sunnah status is emphasized. And the imam should not come with supplication at the taslim if the people are bored with it, nor should he leave it entirely, so he supplicates with a short one to achieve the sunnah. And Tarawih is not made up at all after its time, individually or in congregation, according to the most correct opinion, because making up is specific to obligatory acts. And if one makes it up, it becomes a nafl mustahabb, not Tarawih. And it is a sunnah of the time, not a sunnah of the fast, according to the most correct opinion. So whoever becomes eligible for prayer at the end of the day, Tarawih is recommended for him, like the menstruating woman when she becomes pure, and the traveler, and the sick person who broke his fast. His saying (and he should beware of hasty recitation) is found in the copies we have with the unmarked dal, and in al-Dur with the dotted dhal, and it is explained in al-Qamus as speed of speech and reading. His saying (and leaving tarteel) is in al-Qamus: he arranged speech tarteelan, meaning he composed it well. The intended meaning is that he does not give the recitation its due. His saying (and other things) like leaving ta'awwudh and tasmiyah, and leaving rest between each two tawrihas. The karahah in the three mentioned in his speech is tahrimi, and in others it is tanzihi, because they are in exchange for leaving sunan. His saying (and similarly he does not leave the praise) whether he is an imam, follower, or alone. It is reasoned in al-Fath that sunan are not abandoned for congregations. His saying (because of its being obligatory according to some) is Abu Muti' al-Balkhi, a student of the Great Imam, may Allah be pleased with him. And it is said it is wajib. His saying (and the imam does not come with supplication) i.e., long supplication, as he said: so he supplicates with a short one. His saying (and Tarawih is not made up) because it is not more emphatic than the sunnah of Maghrib and Isha, and they are not made up, so it is more deserving of not being made up. His saying (according to the most correct opinion) its opposite has preceded. His saying (and the traveler and the sick) are not correctly couched with the menstruating woman because they are eligible for it before the end of the day. The expression in the Sharh is better, where he said: And the most correct is that it is a sunnah of the time because of his saying: I have prescribed for you the night prayer, so much so that the sick person who broke his fast, the traveler, the menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum when they become pure, and the disbeliever when he becomes Muslim at the end of the day, Tarawih is recommended for them. So how is the resident, healthy, fasting person excused in leaving it? In al-Qunyah: if they leave the congregation in the obligatory prayer, they do not have the right to pray Tarawih in congregation because it is subsidiary to it. And if one did not pray it with an imam, he may pray witr with him, just as he may pray Tarawih with an imam and witr with another, according to the correct view. And it is disliked for the follower to sit in Tarawih, and when the imam intends to bow, he stands. The apparent expression of the Sharh indicates the proven dislike even if he entered into the imam's prayer, because he reasoned it with what involves opposing the imam, and what involves the statement of the obligation of standing in Tarawih. And it is disliked when sleep overcomes, so one should go until he wakes up, because in prayer with sleep there is carelessness, heedlessness, and leaving of reflection. This is not specific to Tarawih, but rather all prayers are like this. And Allah, the Glorious and Exalted, knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah, the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (hashiyah) on Maraqi al-Falah addressing multiple rulings of Tarawih prayer. The author first discusses the amount of Quran recitation in Tarawih. The base text states that the imam recites approximately ten verses per rak'ah, citing the practice of Abu Hanifa who would complete the Quran many times during Ramadan. However, the key ruling is that if the congregation becomes bored (malla al-qawm), the imam should shorten the recitation to prevent them from leaving. This is the preferred view (al-mukhtar) because, as stated, increasing the number of congregation members is more rewardable than prolonging the recitation. A hadith is cited where the Prophet (saw) forbade Ubayy ibn Ka'b from lengthening the recitation. Furthermore, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to recite only the Fatiha or less than three verses or their equivalent (one long verse or two medium verses) after the Fatiha because it entails abandoning a wajib (obligatory) element. The text then addresses the issue of sending salawat upon the Prophet in the tashahhud. According to the Hanafi school, it is an emphatic sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada), not obligatory, though some other mujtahids (including Imam al-Shafi'i) consider it an obligatory integral (fard). The commentary emphasizes that despite this difference, the Hanafi position is to not abandon it. Next, the commentary warns against certain undesirable practices in Tarawih: hasty recitation (hadrama), lack of tarteel (proper articulation), and negligence in straightening the postures (ta'dil al-arkan). If the congregation becomes bored with even the shortened version, the imam should not abandon the sunnah acts like the opening praise (thana') and the tasbih of ruku' and sujud, as these are emphatic sunan or even considered wajib by some (like Abu Muti' al-Balkhi). The imam should avoid long supplications at the end if it bores the people, but should not omit them entirely; rather, he should offer short supplications. Finally, the commentary clarifies that Tarawih cannot be made up (qada) after its prescribed time (the nights of Ramadan), whether individually or in congregation, because qada is specific to obligatory acts. If one prays it later, it becomes a supererogatory prayer (nafl), not Tarawih. This is because Tarawih is a sunnah of the time (the nights of Ramadan), not a sunnah of fasting. Therefore, those who become eligible for prayer at the end of the day, such as a menstruating woman who becomes pure, a traveler, or a sick person who broke his fast, are recommended to pray Tarawih. The passage ends with various minor rulings, including dislike of sitting while the imam of Tarawih stands, and dislike of praying while sleepy.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarawih): The special night prayers during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs (in the Hanafi school) performed after Isha.
الهدرمة (al-hadrama): Hasty recitation without proper articulation and tarteel.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory act that is between fard and sunnah; omission is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer in the same way as missing a pillar. In this passage, reciting at least three verses after Fatiha in Tarawih is considered wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible and fine.
B) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
C) It invalidates the rak'ah.
D) It is sunnah to do so.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih recitation must include at least three short verses after Fatiha; omission is makruh tahrimi, and missed Tarawih cannot be made up but becomes nafl.

Rulings on Tarawih Prayer and Related Sunan
Hashiya explaining Tarawih rulings and sunan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed Tarawih and identify the emphasized sunan that should not be omitted in prayer.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a sunnah of time, not made up after its time; its sunan are not abandoned even for congregation weariness.

This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi clarifies several practical rulings for the imam and congregation concerning Tarawih. It emphasizes that Tarawih is a sunnah of the nights of Ramadan, not a sunnah of fasting, and therefore cannot be made up later because qada is only for obligatory acts. It also warns against hurried recitation and omitting the opening supplication and tasbeeh, which are emphasized sunan even if the congregation is weary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of Tarawih
According to the passage, Tarawih is a sunnah of time, not of fasting. Understand that it is linked to the time (nights of Ramadan), not to the state of fasting.
2
Determine the ruling on qada
The passage states Tarawih is not made up after its time. The reason given: qada is a characteristic of wajib acts. Tarawih is sunnah, so it cannot be made up. If one prays it later, it becomes nafl, not Tarawih.
Key phrase: 'لأن القضاء من خصائص الواجبات' (because qada is a characteristic of wajib acts).
3
Understand exceptions and applicability
Those who become eligible for prayer at the end of the day (e.g., a menstruating woman who becomes pure, a traveler, a sick person) should still pray Tarawih if they can, because it is sunnah of time.
Reinforces that Tarawih is not tied to fasting.
4
Analyze the rulings on sunan
The passage warns against hdrma (hurried recitation), leaving tarteel, and not performing pillars properly. It also stresses that thana (opening supplication) at the start of each pair and tasbeeh in ruku/sujud should not be omitted even if the congregation is weary.
These sunan are emphasized; abandoning them without excuse is makruh tahrimi.
5
Apply the imam's discretion on dua
The imam should not make a long dua at the end if the congregation is tired, but should not omit it entirely. He should make a short dua to fulfill the sunnah.
Balance between sunnah and consideration for the congregation.

Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage from the hashia of al-Tahtawi explains several rulings related to tarawih prayer. The author warns against hdrma (rapid recitation), leaving tarteel, and not properly performing the pillars. He states that even if the congregation is weary, the imam should not omit the opening supplication (thana') at the start of each pair of rak'ahs, nor the tasbeeh in ruku' and sujud, as these are emphasized sunnas. Regarding the imam's supplication at the end of tarawih, he should not make a long dua if the congregation is tired, but should not omit it entirely; rather he should make a short one. Then a key ruling: tarawih is not to be made up after its time, whether individually or in congregation, because qada' is only for obligatory acts. If one does pray it after its time, it counts as a voluntary nafl, not as tarawih. Tarawih is a sunnah of the time (the nights of Ramadan), not a sunnah of fasting. Hence, those who become eligible for prayer at the end of the day, such as a menstruating woman who becomes pure, a traveler, or a sick person who broke his fast, should pray tarawih. The commentary then elaborates on each point: the definition of hdrma, the meaning of tarteel, the ruling that leaving these is makruh tahrimi for the three mentioned and makruh tanzihi for others. It also notes that some scholars (Abu Muti' al-Balkhi) considered tasbeeh as obligatory, but the madhhab holds it as emphasized sunna. Regarding tarawih, the commentator cites the principle that it is not more emphasized than the sunna of Maghrib and Isha, which are not made up. He also discusses that a traveler and sick person are different from a menstruating woman because they were already eligible before the end of the day. The text further mentions from al-Qunyah that if people leave the congregation in the obligatory prayer, they should not pray tarawih in congregation because it is a follower of the obligatory. It is also disliked for a follower to sit during tarawih when the imam intends to bow. Prayer during drowsiness is also disliked. The overall lesson clarifies the nuanced rulings of tarawih within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الهدرمة (al-hadramah): Rapid, indistinct speech or recitation, especially in prayer; considered disliked (makruh).
الترتيل (al-tartil): Measured, deliberate recitation of the Quran, giving each letter its due.
التراويح (al-tarawih): Night prayers during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs, performed in congregation as an emphasized sunnah.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time; in Hanafi usul, qada is specifically for wajib acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is only recommended and not obligatory.
B) Because qada is a characteristic of wajib acts, and Tarawih is sunnah.
C) Because the congregation is usually tired.
D) Because it is considered a nafl prayer.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a sunnah of the nights of Ramadan and is not made up after its time; if performed later, it becomes nafl.

Prayer Inside and on Top of the Ka'bah: Validity and Proofs
Commentary expanding on prayer rulings in and on the Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Ka'bah and explain the legal reasoning (istidlal) from the Quranic verse and the hadith of Bilal (ra).

Core Idea
Prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid; on top is valid but makruh — the qibla includes the space above the building.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a unique scenario: praying inside the Ka'bah itself, or on its roof. The passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the definition of qibla according to the Hanafi school, the evidence for the validity of such prayers, and the etiquette-related ruling of dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) for praying atop the sacred structure. Understanding this ruling sharpens one's grasp of the conditions of prayer and the scope of the qibla requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of qibla
The passage states that qibla includes the area of the Ka'bah and its air space up to the sky, not just the building.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that the air space has the same ruling as the ground.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The verse (2:125) commands purifying the House for prayer, implying prayer is valid within it. This is a dalil from the Quran that the Hanafi school uses to support the validity of prayer inside the Ka'bah.
The command 'tahhira bayti' (purify My House) indicates that prayer can take place there.
3
Examine the hadith proof
Bilal (ra) prayed inside the Ka'bah. The Hanafi rule that this applies to both nafl and fard because the conditions of validity (facing qibla) are met.
The hadith is cited as evidence that the Prophet (saw) allowed prayer inside, though Bilal's prayer was nafl.
4
Understand the ruling on prayer on top
Prayer on top of the Ka'bah is valid but makruh tanzihi due to disrespect (isā'at al-adab).
The dislike is for etiquette, not because the prayer is invalid.
5
Note the consequence of turning away
If one prays two rak'ahs facing different directions, the prayer is invalid because it turns away from the qibla without necessity.
This applies even inside the Ka'bah, as the entire interior is qibla direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الصلاة في الكعبة وهي البيت الحرام سميت كعبة لتربعها أو لنتوئها، ومنه الكاعب لمن ارتفع نهدها، واختلف في المضاعفة الحاصلة في الصلاة، فقيل : خاصة بالعمل فيها أي في المسجد العتيق وهو ما حولها المحدد بوضع الرخام فيه ، وقيل : تحصل بالعمل في كل بقاع المسجد، وقيل: بالعمل في كل الحرم. قوله : (عندنا) وعند الشافعي اسم للبناء والبقعة حموي عن البرجندي. قوله : (وليس بناؤها قبلة لأنه لو صلى على جبل أبي قبيس لا يكون بين يديه شيء من بناء الكعبة، وصحت صلاته كذا في الشرح قوله : (ولذا حين أزيل البناء) أي في زمن عبد الله بن الزبير قوله : (الآية) أي اقرأ الآية وتمامها للطائفين والعاكفين والركع السجود. قوله : (ظاهر في صحتها فيه إذ لا معنى لتطهير المكان لأجل الصلاة، وهي لا تجوز في ذلك المكان في الشرح والدليل على صحة الصلاة فيها مطلقاً من السنة حديث بلال رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه دخل البيت، وصلى فيه وصلاته وإن كانت نفلاً فالفرض في معناه فيما هو من شرائط الجواز دون الأركان، ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها بوجود استقبال القبلة. أفاده في الشرح، ومتى صارت قبلة فاستدبارها في الصلاة من غير ضرورة يكون مفسداً، فلو صلى ركعة إلى جهته، وركعة إلى جهة أخرى لا تصح صلاته لأنه صار مستديراً للجهة التي صارت قبلة في حقه بيقين من غير ضرورة بخلاف المتحري إذا تبدل تحريه أفاده السيد والمراد بالاستدبار ترك الإستقبال، وإلا فقد ينتقل من جهة إلى جهة من غير استدبار قوله : (لما ذكرنا) أي القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة، وهوائها إلى عنان السماء قوله : (الإساءة الأدب) يفيد أن الكراهة للتنزيه قوله وترك تعظيمها أي ظاهراً وإلا فهو معظم لها باطناً وإلا كفر . قوله : حاشية الطحطاوي/ م٢٧
Chapter on prayer in the Ka'bah. It is the sacred house. It is called Ka'bah because of its square shape or its prominence. From it is al-ka'ab (a young woman whose breast has risen). There is a difference of opinion regarding the multiplication of reward obtained in prayer: some say it is specific to action in the 'atiq mosque (the ancient house) which is what is around it defined by the placement of marble; some say it is obtained by action in every area of the mosque; some say by action in the entire sanctuary. His statement: (according to us) while according to al-Shafi'i it is a name for the building and the area. ... (explanation of qibla etc.) ... His statement: (the verse) i.e. read the verse, and its completion is 'for those who circumambulate, those who stay in i'tikaf, and those who bow and prostrate.' His statement: (apparent in its validity therein) since there is no meaning to purifying a place for prayer if prayer is not permissible in that place. And the proof from the sunnah for the validity of prayer inside it absolutely is the hadith of Bilal (may Allah be pleased with him) that he entered the House and prayed in it. And his prayer was nafl, but the fard is similar in terms of conditions of validity, not pillars. Because it is a prayer that has gathered its conditions by the existence of facing the qibla. ... And whenever something becomes qibla, turning one's back to it without necessity invalidates the prayer. So if one prays one rak'ah facing one direction and another rak'ah facing another direction, his prayer is not valid because he has turned away from the direction that became qibla for him by certainty without necessity. ... His statement: (due to what we mentioned) i.e. qibla is the name for the limited area of the Ka'bah and its air up to the sky. His statement: (bad manners) indicates that the dislike is tanzihi (not tahrimi). And he said: and leaving its veneration, i.e. outwardly, otherwise he venerates it inwardly, otherwise it would be kufr.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on prayer in the Ka'bah. It begins with a lexicographical note on the word 'Ka'bah' and discusses the multiplication of reward for prayers in the Sacred Mosque. The commentator then addresses the definition of qibla: according to the Hanafi school, qibla includes both the building of the Ka'bah and its space up to the heavens, while according to al-Shafi'i, it is only the building. Evidence for the Hanafi view is that the Companions prayed facing the empty place when the Ka'bah was demolished, and they did not set up a partition. Also, prayer on Mount Abu Qubais is valid even though no part of the building is in front. The passage then proves the validity of prayer inside the Ka'bah using both the Quranic command to purify the House (implying prayer in it) and the hadith of Bilal who prayed inside. The ruling applies to both fard and nafl. However, it is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to pray on top of the Ka'bah due to disrespect. The text also discusses that turning away from the qibla without necessity invalidates prayer, and clarifies that if one prays two rak'ahs facing different directions, it is invalid. The commentary distinguishes between tahrimi and tanzihi dislike for certain actions.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-ka'bah): The sacred House in Mecca, the qibla for Muslims.
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction of prayer, which is the Ka'bah and its air space up to the sky.
الاستقبال (al-istiqbal): Facing the qibla, a condition for prayer validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying on top of the Ka'bah?
A) Valid
B) Valid but makruh tanzihi
C) Invalid
D) Valid only for nafl

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid because the qibla includes the space; prayer on top is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to etiquette.

Definition of Qibla and Prayer Inside the Kaaba
Defines qibla and rules on prayer inside/on top of Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qibla and derive the ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Kaaba using the proofs provided.

Core Idea
The qibla is the entire precinct of the Kaaba and its airspace, making prayer inside valid.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi position on what constitutes the qibla. It addresses a common question: can one pray inside the Kaaba? The answer is yes, and the reasoning hinges on the definition of qibla as the area, not the structure. We will examine the proofs and the nuance of the dislike for praying on top.

Guided Path
1
Define the qibla in the Hanafi school
Identify that the qibla is the defined area (buq'a) of the Kaaba and its airspace, not the building itself. Note the key phrase 'بقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها'.
This definition is unique to the Hanafi school; Shafi'i includes the building as well.
2
State the condition for prayer regarding qibla
Recognize that facing the qibla is a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer. The condition is fulfilled by facing any part of the precinct or its airspace.
3
Derive the ruling for prayer inside the Kaaba
Using the definition, conclude that prayer inside the Kaaba is valid (sahih) because the entire interior is part of the qibla. Support with the Quranic command to purify the House and the hadith of Bilal.
The text explicitly says: 'صح فرض ونفل فيها'.
4
Derive the ruling for prayer on top of the Kaaba
Similarly, prayer on top is valid because the airspace is included. However, note the dislike (karaha tanzihiyya) due to lack of respect by being above the Kaaba.
The dislike is tanzihi, not tahrimi, so the prayer is still valid.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference and the nature of the dislike
Compare with the Shafi'i view that qibla includes the building as well. Understand that the Hanafi dislike for praying on top is only tanzihi, so it does not affect validity.
Both schools agree on validity of prayer inside, but differ on definition of qibla.

Source Text

باب الصلاة في الكعبة قال الله قدمنا من شروط الصلاة استقبال القبلة وهي الكعبة والشرط استقبال جزء من بقعة الكعبة أو هوائها لأن القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة وهوائها إلى عنان السماء عندنا كما في العناية، وليس بناؤها قبله ولذا حين أزيل البناء صلى الصحابة رضي عنهم إلى البقعة، ولم ينقل عنهم أنهم اتخذوا سترة فلذا صح فرض ونفل فيها أي في داخلها إلى أي جزء منها توجه لقوله تعالى : أن طهرا بيتي الآية لأن الأمر بالتطهير للصلاة فيه ظاهر في صحتها فيه ( وكذا) صح فرض ونفل (فوقها وإن لم يتخذ) مصليهما (سترة) لما ذكرنا لكنه مكروه له الصلاة فوقها الاساءة الأدب باستعلائه (عليها وترك تعظيمها . كذا باب الصلاة يديه شيء من بناء الكعبة، وصحت صلاته كذا في الشرح قوله : (ولذا حين أزيل البناء) أي في زمن عبد الله بن الزبير قوله : (الآية) أي اقرأ الآية وتمامها للطائفين والعاكفين والركع السجود. قوله : (ظاهر في صحتها فيه إذ لا معنى لتطهير المكان لأجل الصلاة، وهي لا تجوز في ذلك المكان في الشرح والدليل على صحة الصلاة فيها مطلقاً من السنة حديث بلال رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه دخل البيت، وصلى فيه وصلاته وإن كانت نفلاً فالفرض في معناه فيما هو من شرائط الجواز دون الأركان، ولأنها صلاة استجمعت شرائطها بوجود استقبال القبلة. أفاده في الشرح، ومتى صارت قبلة فاستدبارها في الصلاة من غير ضرورة يكون مفسداً، فلو صلى ركعة إلى جهته، وركعة إلى جهة أخرى لا تصح صلاته لأنه صار مستديراً للجهة التي صارت قبلة في حقه بيقين من غير ضرورة بخلاف المتحري إذا تبدل تحريه أفاده السيد والمراد بالاستدبار ترك الإستقبال، وإلا فقد ينتقل من جهة إلى جهة من غير استدبار قوله : (لما ذكرنا) أي القبلة اسم لبقعة الكعبة المحدودة، وهوائها إلى عنان السماء قوله : (الإساءة الأدب) يفيد أن الكراهة للتنزيه قوله وترك تعظيمها أي ظاهراً وإلا فهو معظم لها باطناً وإلا كفر . قوله : حاشية الطحطاوي/ م٢٧
Chapter on prayer in the Kaaba. Allah said: We have previously mentioned from the conditions of prayer facing the qibla, and it is the Kaaba, and the condition is facing a part of the area of the Kaaba or its airspace, because the qibla is the name for the defined area of the Kaaba and its airspace up to the sky in our school, as in al-'Inaya. And its building is not the qibla, so when the building was removed, the companions prayed facing the area, and it is not reported that they took a screen. Therefore, obligatory and supererogatory prayer is valid inside it, facing any part of it, due to His saying: 'Purify My House' (Quran 22:26), because the command to purify for prayer indicates its validity in it. And likewise, obligatory and supererogatory prayer is valid on top of it even if the worshipper does not take a screen, for what we mentioned, but it is makruh to pray on top of it due to bad manners by being above it and leaving its veneration. ... (then commentary): The qibla according to us is the area of the Kaaba, and according to al-Shafi'i it is the building and the area. ... The proof from the Sunnah is the hadith of Bilal that he entered the House and prayed, and though his prayer was supererogatory, the obligatory is similar in terms of conditions of validity. ... The dislike is tanzihi (lesser).
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling on prayer inside and on top of the Kaaba. It first defines the qibla as the entire precinct of the Kaaba including its airspace, not just the building itself. This is proven by the practice of the Companions who prayed facing the area when the Kaaba was rebuilt. The ruling that prayer is valid inside the Kaaba is supported by the Quranic command to purify the House and the hadith of Bilal. Prayer on top of the Kaaba is also valid but is makruh tanzih due to disrespect from being above the Kaaba. The commentary explains that the dislike is not prohibitive (tahrimi) but merely discouraged.

Key Terms
قبلة (qibla): The direction of prayer; in Hanafi school, it is the entire defined area of the Kaaba and its airspace up to the sky.
كعبة (ka'ba): The sacred House in Mecca; named for its square shape or protrusion.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyya): Disliked but not forbidden; the act is valid but discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying on top of the Kaaba?
A) Valid and recommended
B) Valid but makruh tanzih
C) Invalid because the roof is not part of the qibla
D) Only valid if one faces the building

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside the Kaaba is valid because the qibla is the entire precinct and airspace; on top is valid but disliked.

Congregational Prayer inside and around the Kaaba
Details the seven scenarios of direction between imam and follower inside the Kaaba and rulings for those outside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven valid scenarios for following an imam inside the Kaaba, explain why the eighth scenario (face-to-face without screen) is disliked, and apply the rulings to cases where followers are outside the Kaaba.

Core Idea
Inside the Kaaba, every direction is qibla, so only direct face-to-face without a screen is disliked; being ahead in direction invalidates.

The Kaaba's unique status as the qibla for Muslims creates special considerations for congregational prayer when the imam and followers are inside or around it. This lesson explores the rules for valid following (iqtida') when directions differ, based on the Hanafi rulings from al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the principle: every side is qibla
Inside the Kaaba, the text states 'كل جانب قبلة' – every direction is qibla. This means differences in orientation do not invalidate the prayer by themselves.
This is unique to inside the Kaaba.
2
List the seven valid scenarios
The text enumerates seven combinations of direction between imam and follower (e.g., follower's face to imam's back, side to side, etc.). All are valid.
See the Arabic passage for the full list.
3
Identify the exception: face-to-face without a screen
When the follower's face directly faces the imam's face without a screen, it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to resemblance to image worship.
This does not invalidate the prayer, but it is disliked.
4
Recognize the invalid scenario: follower ahead
When the follower's back is to the imam's face, the follower is effectively ahead of the imam (taqaddum), which invalidates the following.
This is the only scenario that invalidates inside the Kaaba.
5
Apply to outside cases
When the follower is outside the Kaaba and the imam is inside, it is valid if the door is open or if he can hear the takbir. When forming a circle around the Kaaba, followers who are closer to the Kaaba than the imam and in his direction are invalid because they are ahead.
The condition of door being open is not essential; hearing the takbir suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن جعل ظهره إلى غير وجه إمامه فيها أو فوقها بأن كان وجهه إلى ظهر إمامه، أو إلى جنب إمامه أو ظهره إلى جنب إمامه أو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه أو جنبه إلى وجه إمامه أو جنبه إلى جنب إمامه متوجهاً إلى غير جهته أو وجهه إلى وجه إمامه (صح) اقتداء في هذه الصور السبع إلا أنه يكره إذا قابل وجهه وجه إمامه، وليس بينهما حائل لما تقدم من كراهته لشبهه عبادة الصور وكل جانب ،قبلة والتقدم والتأخر إنما يظهر عند اتحاد الجهة وهي مختلفة في جوف الكعبة وقوله : ( وإن جعل ظهره إلى وجه إمامه لا يصح اقتداؤه تصريح بما علم التزاماً من السابق لايضاح الحكم وذلك لتقدمه على إمامه وصح الاقتداء لمن كان (خارجها بإمام فيها أي في جوفها سواء كان معه جماعة فيها أو لم يكن والباب مفتوح لأنه كقيامه في المحراب في غيرها من المساجد والقيد بفتح الباب اتفاقي فإذا سمع التبليغ، والباب مغلق لا مانع من صحة الاقتداء كما تقدم (وإن تحلقوا حولها والإمام) يصلي (خارجها صح) (إلا) أنه لا جميعهم يصح (لمن كان أقرب إليها) من إمامه وهو (في جهة إمامه) لتقدمه على إمامه وأما من كان أقرب إليها من أمامه وليس في جهته فاقتداؤه صحيح التقدم والتأخر لا يظهر إلا عند اتحاد الجانب المتوجه إليه كل منهما . اقتباس: (متوجهاً إلى غير (جهته بأن يجتمعا في أحد الأركان الأربعة، ويستقبل كل جهة وإنما قيد بغير الجهة لأنه لو كان في جهته يصح بالأولى. قوله : في هذه الصور السبع) وإذا اعتبر في الجنب فالصور التي ذكر هو فيها اليمين والشمال ويمين الإمام ويمين المأموم تزيد على هذا العدد. قوله : (إلا أنه يكره إذا قابل الخ) ظاهره كراهة التحريم لما يأتي من التعليل. قوله : (وليس بينهما حائل) أما إذا وجد فلا كراهة لعدم التشبه بعبادة الصور. قوله : (وكل جانب قبلة الخ) اعلم أنه لا بد في صلاة الجماعة من استقبال الجميع القبلة، وأن لا يتقدم المأموم على إمامه، فأشار إلى الأول بقوله : وكل جانب قبلة وأشار إلى الثاني بقوله والتقدم والتأخر الخ. قوله: (وهي مختلفة في جوف الكعبة) يعم الصلاة فيها وفوقها فإن الجوف موجود فيهما . قوله: (وذلك لتقدمه على إمامه أي في جهته واسم الإشارة راجع إلى عدم الصحة قوله : (وصح الإقتداء الخ) أي إذا وجدت الشروط، أما إذا فقد بعضها كما إذا خرج عن استقبال العين فإنه لا يصح الإقتداء كالمنفرد قوله : (أو لم يكن وهل يكره ذلك لانفراد الإمام في محل عال السابقة بعينها صحة، وفساداً إلا أنها ذكرت فيما تقدم إذا كان الصلاة فيها، أو فوقها، وهنا ذكرت فيما إذا تحلقوا حولها . قوله: (لا يظهر) الأولى لا يظهر أن أو الواو بمعنى أو أن كلا منهما لازم للآخر لأنه يلزم من التقدم التأخر، وعكسه فهما بمنزلة شيء واحد فلذا أفرد الضمير قوله : (المتوجه) بصيغة اسم الفاعل، وكل فاعله والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And whoever places his back to a direction other than the face of his imam inside or on top [of the Kaaba], such that his face is towards the back of his imam, or towards the side of his imam, or his back towards the side of his imam, or his back towards the back of his imam, or his side towards the face of his imam, or his side towards the side of his imam, turning to a different direction, or his face towards the face of his imam — the following is valid in these seven scenarios, except that it is disliked when his face faces his imam's face without a screen, due to the previously mentioned dislike of resembling the worship of images. And every side is qibla. Advance and delay only appear when the direction is unified, and it differs inside the Kaaba. And his saying: 'And if he places his back to the face of his imam, his following is not valid' is an explicit statement of what is implied by the previous, to clarify the ruling, and that is because he is ahead of his imam. And following is valid for one who is outside the Kaaba with an imam inside, whether there is a congregation inside or not, and the door is open, because it is like standing in the mihrab in other mosques. The condition of the door being open is coincidental; if he hears the takbir and the door is closed, there is no prevention. And if they form a circle around the Kaaba while the imam prays outside, the following is valid for all except for those who are closer to the Kaaba than his imam and are in his imam's direction, because they are ahead. As for those closer to the Kaaba but not in his direction, their following is valid. ... (commentary continues explaining the seven scenarios and the rulings).
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage details the rules for congregational prayer when the imam and followers are inside or on top of the Kaaba, or when the imam is outside. The text lists seven scenarios where the directions of the imam and follower differ, but the follower is still valid as long as they do not face each other directly without a screen (which is disliked due to resembling image worship). The key principle is that every direction inside the Kaaba is qibla, so differences in orientation do not invalidate the prayer. However, if the follower places his back to the imam's face, it is invalid because the follower is effectively ahead. For those outside following an imam inside, it is valid if the door is open (or closed if they hear the takbir). For those surrounding the Kaaba with an imam outside, those closer to the Kaaba than the imam and in his direction are invalid because they are ahead; others are valid.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer; the act of the follower.
تقدم (taqaddum): The follower being ahead of the imam in direction, which invalidates following.
كراهة تحريمية (karaha tahrimiyya): Prohibitively disliked; closer to haram.
صورة (surah): Scenario or form; here referring to one of the seven positional arrangements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario is the follower's prayer invalid when inside the Kaaba?
A) When the follower's face is towards the imam's back
B) When the follower's back is towards the imam's back
C) When the follower's back is towards the imam's face
D) When the follower's side is towards the imam's side

Key Takeaway
Inside the Kaaba, following is valid across different directions as long as the follower is not ahead of the imam; face-to-face without a screen is disliked but not invalid.

Following an Imam Inside or Outside the Ka'bah
Refines iqtida' rulings for Ka'bah scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for iqtida' when the imam is inside the Ka'bah and identify when the prayer is valid, invalid, or disliked.

Core Idea
Inside the Ka'bah every direction is qibla, but face-to-face with no barrier is disliked and being ahead invalidates.

The Ka'bah is the qibla, but when praying inside it, the direction becomes relative. This lesson refines the rules of following the imam in such unique circumstances. It covers scenarios like facing different directions, being outside while the imam is inside, and circling the Ka'bah. The focus is on preserving the two essential conditions of congregational prayer: uniform qibla orientation and the follower not being ahead of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on facing different directions inside the Ka'bah
Inside the Ka'bah, each side is a valid qibla. When the imam and follower face different sides, the iqtida' is valid as long as they are not face-to-face without a barrier. Determine the hukm: valid but disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the face-to-face case.
The dislike is due to resemblance to image worship (shibbuh 'ibadat al-suwar).
2
Understand the condition of not being ahead
The follower must not be ahead of the imam in direction. Inside the Ka'bah, precedence only matters when both face the same direction. If they face different sides, the follower is not considered ahead even if physically closer.
If the follower places his back to the imam's face, it is invalid because he is ahead.
3
Apply the ruling for follower outside the Ka'bah with imam inside
It is valid provided the follower faces the qibla (the direction of the Ka'bah) and the imam is inside. The door being open is incidental; validity remains even if closed as long as the follower hears the notification.
The imam's position inside is likened to standing in the mihrab of a mosque.
4
Analyze the scenario of followers circling around the Ka'bah with imam outside
All followers around the Ka'bah can follow the imam outside, except those who are closer to the Ka'bah than the imam and are in the same direction as the imam. Those individuals are ahead and their iqtida' is invalid.
Followers not in the imam's direction are valid because precedence doesn't apply when directions differ.

Commentary
This passage is a hashia (super-commentary) on the text of Maraqi al-Falah, refining the rulings on following the imam when the prayer is inside or around the Ka'bah. The author explains the seven scenarios where following is valid even when directions differ. He clarifies that facing the imam face-to-face without a barrier is disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it resembles the worship of images. Inside the Ka'bah, every direction is valid as qibla, but precedence/lateness only matter when the direction is the same. The text then addresses the case where the follower is outside the Ka'bah and the imam inside: it is valid provided the follower maintains qibla direction, with the door open being incidental. When followers circle around the Ka'bah with the imam outside, only those not closer to the Ka'bah than the imam in the imam's direction are valid; those closer are invalid due to being ahead. The commentary resolves ambiguities in the matn, emphasizing that the conditions for congregational prayer (uniform qibla and no follower ahead) are preserved.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer; the act of a follower (ma'mum) conforming to the imam's actions.
جهة (jihah): Direction; specifically the direction each person faces for prayer.
شبه عبادة الصور (shibbuh 'ibadat al-suwar): Resemblance to the worship of images; a reason for dislike (karahah) because it mimics idolatry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The door must be locked.

Key Takeaway
Following an imam inside the Ka'bah is valid with conditions: no being ahead, and face-to-face without a barrier is disliked.

Definition and Legal Effects of Travel (Safar)
Defining travel and its legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define travel (safar) legally and state the Hanafi ruling on concessions for sinful travel.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, all types of travel — obedient, permissible, or sinful — entitle the traveller to legal concessions.

This passage opens the chapter on the traveller's prayer by establishing what constitutes travel (safar) in Islamic law. The author defines travel both linguistically and legally, then highlights a key point of difference: whether sinful travel still grants the traveller concessions. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly applying rulings on shortening prayer, breaking fast, and other travel-related dispensations.

Guided Path
1
Extract the linguistic and legal definitions
Identify the author's definitions: in language, safar is 'cutting distance' or prolonged departure; in sacred law, it is departure from one's inhabited homeland with a specific minimum distance. Note the emphasis on 'distance' as a key element.
The legal definition sets the threshold for when travel concessions apply.
2
Identify the three categories of travel
List the three types: travel of obedience (hajj, jihad), permissible travel (trade), and travel of disobedience (highway robbery). Understand that the first two are agreed upon as causes for concessions, while the third is disputed.
This classification is crucial for determining whether the traveller benefits from rukhsah.
3
Compare the Hanafi position on sinful travel
Note that the Hanafi school (along with al-Awza'i, al-Thawri, Dawud, al-Muzani, and some Malikis) holds that even sinful travel entitles the traveller to concessions. Contrast with Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad who deny concessions for sinful travel.
The basis: rukhsah is tied to the act of travel itself, not the intention behind it.
4
List the legal effects of travel
Enumerate the concessions (rukhsah) mentioned: obligation to shorten four-rak'ah prayers, permissibility of breaking fast in Ramadan, extension of masah to three days, dropping of Jumu'ah, 'Id prayers, and Udhiyah, and prohibition of a free woman traveling without a mahram.
These effects are the practical consequences of being a traveller.
5
Analyse the debate on qasr as azimah or rukhsah
Understand that qasr is a concession of removal (rukhsat al-isqat): the second pair of rak'ahs is dropped entirely, so the traveller's obligation is only two rak'ahs. The author sides with al-Fath, stating that the dispute over whether qasr is azimah or rukhsah is mistaken because it is both in different respects.
This nuance clarifies that qasr is not optional but the required prayer for a traveller.

Source Text

Travel in language is cutting distance, and in sacred law it is a determined distance with a specific travel. He explained it with his saying: (The least) period of (travel by which) the travel (changes) the rulings, which are the obligation of shortening the prayer as a concession of removal. Know that the concession is called because it is a travel intended to disclose, i.e., reveals the character of men. So the mutual interaction is not according to its usual meaning because it occurs only between two, and this is from one. End. His saying: The least period of travel by which the rulings change. Travel is of three types: travel of obedience like Hajj and jihad, permissible travel like trade, and travel of disobedience like highway robbery. The first two are causes for concession by agreement. As for the last, similarly according to us, and al-Awza'i, al-Thawri, Dawud, al-Muzani, and some Malikis said so, contrary to Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, for they said travel of disobedience does not yield concession because it is established as relief, and whatever is like that does not attach to what necessitates severity, namely disobedience. Mentioned by 'Allamah Nuh and in al-Halabi al-Kabir. For the traveller there are rulings in which he differs from the resident, like the permissibility of breaking fast in Ramadan, the extension of the wiping period to three days, the dropping of Jumu'ah, the two 'Ids, and Udhiyah, and among them is shortening the four-rak'ah prayers. End. His saying: (and they are the obligation of shortening the prayer) the pronoun refers to the rulings, and this interpretation is not good; the better is what in the sharh where he said: they are the obligation of shortening the prayer, permissibility of breaking fast, extension of wiping period to three days, dropping the obligation of Jumu'ah, the two 'Ids and Udhiyah, and prohibition of a free woman traveling without a mahram, and other than that. End. His saying: (as a concession of removal) better is that he say: it is a concession of removal, i.e., removing the ruling entirely not to a substitute, for the second pair of rak'ahs is dropped from him such that he does not make it up after settling, so the obligatory prayer for him is two rak'ahs. Thus there is no change from difficulty to ease in his case. Hence it appears that the concession of removal and the determination are one thing in extension although they differ in intension. Therefore it was said in al-Fath: whoever reports a dispute among the mashayikh that shortening is determination (azimah) according to us or concession has made a mistake, because he who says: concession...

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on the traveller's prayer, defining travel (safar) both linguistically and legally. Linguistically, it means 'cutting distance' or prolonged departure. Legally, it is a specific distance (later defined) that triggers concessions (rukhsah). The author discusses the three types of travel: obedience (hajj, jihad), permissible (trade), and disobedience (highway robbery). For the Hanafi school, all three types permit concessions, contrary to some other schools that deny concessions for sinful travel. The legal effects of travel include: obligation to shorten four-rak'ah prayers, permissibility of breaking fast in Ramadan, extension of masah (wiping over socks) to three days, dropping of Jumu'ah, 'Id prayers, and Udhiyah, and prohibition of a free woman traveling without a mahram. The commentary also clarifies a subtle point: the 'concession of removal' (rukhsat al-isqat) means the second pair of rak'ahs is entirely dropped, not replaced, so the default prayer becomes two rak'ahs. This leads to the debate about whether qasr is azimah or rukhsah; the author sides with those who say it is both in different senses, rejecting any dispute as mistaken.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Travel; legally, departure from one's inhabited homeland with a specific minimum distance (about 48 miles or 3 days' journey).
رخصة (rukhsah): Concession; a relaxation of a normal ruling due to necessity or hardship.
قصر (qasr): Shortening of four-rak'ah prayers to two for travellers.
عزيمة (azimah): Determination; a ruling that remains in its original form without concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only permissible travel (e.g., trade).
C) All types of travel, including sinful travel.
D) Only travel that is not sinful.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines travel by a minimum distance and grants all travellers—regardless of intention—the concessions of shortened prayer, breaking fast, and other relaxations.

Definition and Legal Types of Travel and Its Effect on Rulings
Defines travel, its types, and lists rulings that change due to travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define travel (safar) in Hanafi law, distinguish its three types, explain why qasr is a license of removal (rukhsat al-isqat) that is also the determined obligation (azimah) for the traveler, and state the Hanafi position on travel of disobedience granting licenses.

Core Idea
Travel changes rulings: qasr is a wajib license that removes the original obligation, making two rak'at the fard for the traveler.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi defines the legal concept of travel (safar) and its effect on prayer, fasting, and other obligations. It clarifies that qasr is a unique license called 'rukhsat al-isqat' which completely removes the original obligation without substitution, and it addresses a cross-madhhab dispute over whether travel of disobedience grants such licenses.

Guided Path
1
Define travel linguistically and legally
Analyze the linguistic meaning (cutting distance, uncovering) and the legal definition: departure from the built-up area of one's hometown with a specific distance (three days' journey).
Hanafi school defines travel by distance, not intention alone.
2
Identify the three types of travel
Travel of obedience (hajj, jihad), permissible travel (trade), and travel of disobedience (highway robbery). Note which types are agreed upon as causes for licenses.
First two are agreed; third is disputed.
3
List the rulings that change for the traveler
Name the key differences: permission to break fast, extended wiping period, omission of Jumu'ah, Eid, and Udhiyah, and shortening of four-rak'ah prayers.
Qasr is highlighted as 'luzum' (obligation).
4
Understand rukhsat al-isqat
Define a license that removes the original obligation entirely without substituting another. For qasr, the second two rak'at are dropped, so the fard becomes two rak'at.
Thus qasr is both a license and an azimah in effect, since there is no choice.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position on travel of disobedience
Hanafis grant licenses even for sinful travel, contrary to Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad. Note the reasoning: licenses are attached to the act of travel itself, not its moral status.
This dispute has practical implications for fatwa.
